Rulings for the Dying Person and Immediately After Death
States rulings and proofs for dying person's care

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three sunnah actions for a dying person and identify the Hanafi level of obligation (mustahabb) with evidence from the hadith.

Core Idea
Turning to Qibla, talqeen, and closing eyes are mustahabb, not wajib — based on ahad hadith and practice.

In this lesson, we examine the rulings for a person on their deathbed and immediately after death. Al-Quduri presents three actions: turning the dying person to face the Qibla on the right side, prompting them with the shahada (talqeen), and after death binding the jaws and closing the eyes. The commentary provides proofs from the Qur'an, hadith, and practice of the salaf, demonstrating that these acts are recommended (mustahabb) but not obligatory.

Guided Path
1
Identify the actions
Recognize the three actions mentioned: turning to Qibla, talqeen, and post-death care (binding jaws and closing eyes).
2
Note the hukm level
Understand that each action is mustahabb (recommended) in the Hanafi school, not wajib. The Urdu commentary uses the term 'mustahabb' explicitly.
3
Locate the proof for talqeen
The hadith 'Laqqinu mawtakum la ilaha illa Allah' is the primary proof. Note it is a hadith ahad; in Hanafi usul, a command from a ahad hadith indicates recommendation unless there is a qarinah for obligation.
Muslim no. 917
4
Understand the evidence for turning to Qibla
The proof is from the Prophet's instruction on sleeping position (Bukhari, Muslim) and the practice of Ibrahim an-Nakha'i. The action is based on qiyas: the deceased will be laid facing Qibla in the grave.
5
Recognize the post-death actions
Binding jaws and closing eyes are based on the Prophet's action when Abu Salamah died (Muslim no. 920). The Prophet said the eyes follow the soul when it is taken.

Source Text

بَابُ الْجِنَائِزِ
وَإِذَا احْتُضِرَ الرَّجُلُ وُجّهَ وَجْهُهُ إِلَى الْقِبْلَةِ عَلَى شِقّهِ الْأَيْمَن قَوْلُهُ : وَلُقِنَ الشَّهَادَتَيْنِ – فَإِذَا مَاتَ شَدُّوا حَيَيْهِ وَغَمَّضُوا عَيْنَيْهِ لوجه:(1) الآية لثبوت وَإِذَا أَحْتُضِرَ الرَّجُلُ وُجِهَ وَجْهُهُ إِلَى الْقِبْلَةِ \ ﴿وَلَا تُصَلِّ عَلَى أَحَدٍ مِّنْهُم مَّاتَ أَبَدًا وَلَا تَقُمْ عَلَى قَبْرِهِ إِنَّهُمْ كَفَرُوا بِاللَّهِ وَرَسُولِهِ وَمَاتُوا وَهُمْ فَاسِقُونَ (سورة التوبة، أيت نمبر 84)
وجه : (۲) الحديث لثبوت وَإِذَا احْتُضِرَ الرَّجُلُ وُجّهَ وَجْهُهُ إِلَى الْقِبْلَةِ \ عَنِ الْبَرَاءِ بْنِ عَازِبٍ قَالَ: قَالَ النَّبِيُّ : إِذَا أَتَيْتَ مَضْجَعَكَ فَتَوَضَّأَ وُضُوءَكَ لِلصَّلَاةِ، ثُمَّ اضْطَجِعْ عَلَى شِقَكَ الْأَيْمَنِ، ثُمَّ قل (بخاري شريف: باب فضل من بات على الوضوء، نمبر 247 مسلم شريف: باب ما يقول عند النوم وأخذ المضجع، نمبر 2710)
وجه (۳) قول التابعي لثبوت وَإِذَا اُحْتُضِرَ الرَّجُلُ وُجّهَ وَجْهُهُ إِلَى الْقِبْلَةِ عَنْ إِبْرَاهِيمَ، قَالَ: «كَانُوا يَسْتَحِبُّونَ أَنْ يُوَجَّهَ الْمَيِّتُ الْقِبْلَةَ إِذَا حَضَرَ» مصنف ابن ابي شيبه: ما قالوا في توجيه الميت، نمبر 10871 مصنف عبدالرزاق باب غسل المرء إذا حضره الموت، وحروف الميت إلى القبلة ،نمبر 6060)
وجه : (۱) الحديث لثبوت وَلُقِنَ الشَّهَادَتَيْنِ \ عَنْ أَبِي هُرَيْرَةَ قَالَ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم : « لَقِنُوا
مَوْتَاكُمْ لَا إِلَهَ إِلَّا اللهُ » (مسلم شریف باب تلقين الموتى لا إله إلا الله، نمبر 917)
وجه: (ا) الحديث لثبوت فَإِذَا مَاتَ شَدُّوا لَحَيَيْهِ وَغَمَّضُوا عَيْنَيْهِ \ عَنْ أُمِّ سَلَمَةَ قَالَتْ: « دَخَلَ رَسُولُ اللهِ الله عَلَى أَبي سَلَمَةَ وَقَدْ شَقَّ بَصَرُهُ، فَأَغْمَضَهُ، ثُمَّ قَالَ: إِنَّ الرُّوحَ إِذَا قُبِضَ تَبِعَهُ الْبَصَرُ (مسلم شريف : باب في إغماض الميت والدعاء له إذا حضر،نمبر920,) اصول : جب کسی شخص کا انتقال ہونے لگے تو اس کو داہنی کروٹ پر قبلہ رو کر دینا مستحب ہے، کیوں کہ قبر میں بھی اسی طرح لٹایا جاتا ہے۔ اصول : جب کسی کا انتقال ہونے لگے تو اس کو کلمہ شہادت کی تلقین کی جائے۔ اس کے دونوں جبڑوں کو کسی پٹی

Chapter of Funerals. And when a man is on his deathbed, his face is turned towards the Qibla on his right side. His statement: and he is prompted with the two testimonies. And when he dies, they bind his jaws and close his eyes. For proof: (1) the verse for proof of turning the dying person's face to the Qibla: {And do not pray over any of them who dies, ever, and do not stand at his grave; indeed they disbelieved in Allah and His Messenger and died while they were defiantly disobedient} (Surah at-Tawbah, verse 84) [note: this verse is actually about not praying for hypocrites; the text uses it as proof that facing Qibla is established? The text seems to mention it but the connection is unclear]. Proof: (2) the hadith for proof of turning the dying person's face to the Qibla: from al-Bara' ibn 'Azib, he said: The Prophet said: When you come to your bed, perform wudu as for prayer, then lie on your right side, then say... (Bukhari: chapter on virtue of sleeping with wudu, no. 247; Muslim: chapter on what to say when sleeping and taking the bed, no. 2710). Proof: (3) the saying of a tabi'i for proof of turning the dying person's face to the Qibla: from Ibrahim, he said: They used to recommend that the dying person be turned to face the Qibla when he is present. (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah: what they said about turning the dying person, no. 10871; Musannaf Abd ar-Razzaq: chapter on washing the person when death is present, and turning the dying person to the Qibla, no. 6060). Proof: (1) the hadith for proof of prompting the two testimonies: from Abu Huraira, he said: The Messenger of Allah said: Prompt your dying ones with 'La ilaha illa Allah' (Muslim: chapter on prompting the dying with La ilaha illa Allah, no. 917). Proof: (a) the hadith for proof of binding his jaws and closing his eyes: from Umm Salamah, she said: The Messenger of Allah entered upon Abu Salamah while his eyesight had [؟] become blurred, so he closed his eyes, then said: Indeed when the soul is taken, the sight follows it. (Muslim: chapter on closing the eyes of the deceased and supplicating for him when he is present, no. 920). Principle: When a person is about to pass away, it is recommended to turn him to the Qibla on his right side, because in the grave he will be laid similarly. Principle: When a person is about to pass away, he should be prompted with the word of shahada. It is recommended to bind both his jaws with a band and close his eyes.
Source pages p. 170

Commentary
This passage from the chapter on funerals (Jana'iz) presents three important sunnah actions for the time of death and immediately after. The author (al-Quduri) states the rulings concisely, and the commentary provides proofs from the Qur'an, hadith, and sayings of the salaf. First, when a person is dying, they should be placed on their right side facing the Qibla. The proof is derived from the Prophet's instruction on sleeping position, and from the practice of the early Muslims (Ibrahim an-Nakha'i). This is mustahabb (recommended), not wajib. Second, the dying person should be prompted (talqeen) to recite the shahada, based on the hadith 'Prompt your dying ones with La ilaha illa Allah'. This is also mustahabb; it is not obligatory, as the hadith is ahad and the command is for recommendation. Third, after death, the jaws should be bound and the eyes closed, following the Prophet's action when Abu Salamah died. The Urdu principles at the end summarize: these actions are mustahabb because of the wisdom of how the deceased will be laid in the grave.

Key Terms
تلقين (talqeen): Prompting the dying person to recite the shahada (La ilaha illa Allah) so that these are their last words.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on prompting the dying person with the shahada?
A) Wajib (obligatory)
B) Mustahabb (recommended)
C) Makruh (disliked)
D) Mubah (permissible)

Key Takeaway
The three actions for the dying and deceased are recommended (mustahabb) based on ahad hadith and practice of the salaf.

Rulings on Sitting Before the Bier and Digging a Lahd
Matn ruling with companion and hadith proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on sitting before the bier is placed and digging a lahd, and identify the hadith evidence for each.

Core Idea
Sitting before the bier is placed is makruh tanzih; digging a lahd is the sunnah, and shaq is only for necessity.

This passage from Al-Quduri's matn begins with two important burial etiquettes: when the funeral party arrives at the grave, and how the grave should be prepared. The rulings are supported by the practice of companions and a clear hadith from the Prophet ﷺ. Understanding these helps avoid common mistakes and ensures the burial follows the sunnah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the first ruling and its evidence
The matn states it is disliked (makruh) for people to sit before the bier is placed. Find the evidence from Abu Hurairah's practice.
This is a statement of a companion (qawl sahabi), which is a valid proof in Hanafi usul.
2
Identify the second ruling and its evidence
The matn states the grave must be dug and made a lahd. Identify the two proofs: Sa'd's instruction and the Prophet's hadith 'The lahd is for us, the shaq is for others'.
The hadith is from Muslim, showing the Prophet explicitly preferred lahd.
3
Understand the exception for shaq
The Urdu note explains that shaq is permissible if the soil is soft and there is fear of collapse. This is a practical concession.
The ruling changes from sunnah to permissible based on necessity (darurah).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فَإِذَا بَلَغُوا إِلَى قَبْرِهِ كُرِهَ لِلنَّاسِ الْقُعُودُ قَبْلَ أَنْ يُوضَعَ عَنْ أَعْنَاقِ الرِّجَالِ وَيُحْفَرُ الْقَبْرُ وَيُلْحَدُ وَيُدْخَلُ الْمَيِّتُ مِمَّا يَلِي الْقِبْلَةَ

وجه (۱) قول الصحابي لثبوت فَإِذَا بَلَغُوا إِلَى قَبْرِهِ كُرِهَ لِلنَّاسِ الْقُعُودُ \ عَنْ أَبِي هُرَيْرَةَ، «أَنَّهُ لَمْ يَكُنْ يَقْعُدُ حَتَّى يُوضَعَ السَّرِيرُ» (مصنف ابن ابي شيبه فِي الرَّجُلِ يَكُونُ مَعَ الْجِنَازَةِ مَنْ قَالَ: لَا يجلس حَتَّى تُوضَعَ، نمبر 11510)

و وجه : (۱) قول الصحابي لثبوت وَيُحْفَرُ الْقَبْرُ وَيُلْحَدُ \ أن سعد بن أبي وقاص قَالَ فِي مَرَضِهِ الَّذِي هَلَكَ فِيهِ : الْخُدُوا لِي خَدًا وَانْصِبُوا عَلَيَّ اللَّبِنَ نَصْبًا . كَمَا صُنعَ بِرَسُولِ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم (مسلم شريف، بَاب فِي اللَّحْدِ وَنَصْبِ اللَّبِنَ عَلَى الْمَيِّتِ، نمبر 966)

وجه:(۲) الحديث لثبوت وَيُحْفَرُ الْقَبْرُ وَيُلْحَدُ عَنْ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ قَالَ: قَالَ النَّبِيُّ صلى الله عليه وسلم: «اللَّحْدُ لَنَا ، وَالشَّقُ لِغَيْرِنَا» (مسلم شريف ، بَابُ مَاجَاءَ فِي قَوْلِ النّبي الله اللَّحْدُ لَنَا، وَالشَّقُّ لِغَيْرِنَا، 1045)

وجه : (1) الحديث لثبوت وَيُدْخَلُ الْمَيِّتُ مِمَّا يَلِي الْقِبْلَةَ \ عَنْ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ، أَنَّ النَّبِيَّ صلى الله عليه وسلم دَخَلَ قَبْرًا لَيْلًا، فَأَسْرِجَ لَهُ سِرَاحٌ، فَأَخَذَهُ مِنْ قِبَلِ القِبْلَةِ، وَقَالَ: «رَحِمَكَ اللَّهُ، إِنْ كُنْتَ لَأَوَّاهًا تَلَّاءً لِلْقُرْآنِ»، وَكَبَّرَ عَلَيْهِ أَرْبَعًا» (سنن الترمذى، بَابُ مَا جَاءَ فِي الدَّفْنِ بِاللَّيْلِ،نمبر1057)

وجه:(1) دليل الشافعي قول التابعي لثبوت وَيُدْخَلُ الْمَيِّتُ مِمَّا يَلِي الْقِبْلَةَ \ عَنْ أَبِي إِسْحَاقَ، قَالَ: أَوْصَى الْحَارِثُ أَنْ يُصَلِّيَ عَلَيْهِ عَبْدُ اللَّهِ بْنُ يَزِيدَ، " فَصَلَّى عَلَيْهِ، ثُمَّ أَدْخَلَهُ الْقَبْرَ مِنْ قِبَلِ رِجْلَي الْقَبْرِ، وَقَالَ: هَذَا مِنَ السُّنَّةِ " (سنن ابوداود، بَابٌ فِي الْمَيِّتِ يُدْخَلُ مِنْ رِجْلَيْهِ، غبر 3211)

اصول: قبر کھودنے کے دو طریقے ہیں: (۱) لحد یعنی بغلی قبر، اور یہی مسنون طریقہ ہے۔ (۲) شق یعنی قبر کو سیدھا کھودا جائے، یہ طریقہ بھی جائز ہے جبکہ مٹی نرم ہو اور قبر بیٹھ جانے کا اندیشہ ہو۔
When they arrive at his grave, it is disliked for the people to sit before it is placed down from the necks of men, and the grave is dug and it is made a lahd, and the deceased is entered from the side facing the qibla. Evidence (1) statement of companion for proof of 'when they arrive...': from Abu Hurairah that he would not sit until the bier was placed. And evidence (1) statement of companion for proof of 'and the grave is dug and it is made a lahd': that Sa'd ibn Abi Waqqas said in his illness in which he died: 'Make a lahd for me and set up bricks over me standing, as was done with the Messenger of Allah.' Evidence (2) hadith for proof of 'and the grave is dug and it is made a lahd': from Ibn Abbas, the Prophet said: 'The lahd is for us, and the shaq is for others.' Evidence (1) hadith for proof of 'and the deceased is entered from the side facing the qibla': from Ibn Abbas that the Prophet entered a grave at night, a lamp was lit for him, so he took him from the direction of the qibla and said... Evidence (1) evidence of al-Shafi'i: statement of a tabi'i for proof of 'and the deceased is entered from the side facing the qibla': from Abu Ishaq, he said: Al-Harith willed that Abdullah ibn Yazid pray over him, so he prayed over him, then he entered him into the grave from the direction of the feet of the grave and said: 'This is from the sunnah.' Principle: there are two methods of digging the grave: (1) lahd, i.e., a side grave, and this is the sunnah method. (2) shaq, i.e., the grave is dug straight, this method is also permissible when the soil is soft and there is fear of the grave collapsing.
Source pages p. 182

Commentary
This passage from Al-Quduri's matn, with its accompanying hadith evidence, details the etiquettes upon arrival at the graveside. It begins by ruling that it is makruh (disliked) for people to sit down before the bier is lowered from the shoulders of the carriers. This is based on the practice of Abu Hurairah. Next, it states that the grave must be dug, and it should be a lahd (a niche dug into the side of the grave cavity) rather than a shaq (a straight trench). The Prophet's hadith explicitly says 'اللحد لنا والشق لغيرنا' (the lahd is for us, the shaq is for others), indicating that the lahd is the sunnah for Muslims. However, the Urdu note clarifies that if the soil is loose and there is a risk of collapse, a shaq is permissible. Finally, the passage stipulates that the deceased should be interred from the qibla side, meaning the body is inserted headfirst from the direction of the qibla. The Hanafi proof is the hadith of Ibn Abbas where the Prophet entered a grave from the qibla side. The Shafi'i school, however, considers it sunnah to enter from the feet side, based on the practice of the companion Al-Harith as reported by Abu Ishaq. The Hanafi response, though not explicitly rebutted here, is that the stronger evidence supports the qibla side, and the Shafi'i proof is a practice of a single companion that does not override the explicit action of the Prophet.

Key Terms
اللَّحْد (al-lahd): A niche dug into the side of the grave cavity to place the body, protecting it from direct soil.
الشَّق (ash-shaqq): A straight trench dug in the bottom of the grave, with the body placed in it and covered with slabs.
كُرِهَ (kurihat): It is disliked (makruh tanzih).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on digging a lahd (side niche) in the grave?
A) It is fard (obligatory)
B) It is sunnah mu'akkadah (highly recommended)
C) It is makruh tanzih (disliked)
D) It is haram (prohibited)

Key Takeaway
Sitting before the bier is placed is disliked, and digging a lahd is the sunnah; shaq is only for necessity.

Entering the Deceased from the Qibla Side: Hanafi vs Shafi'i
Matn ruling with hadith proof and inter-madhhab dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on entering the deceased from the qibla side, cite the hadith evidence, and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
Entering the deceased from the qibla side is sunnah based on the Prophet's action, overriding a companion's practice.

The final part of this passage addresses a common point of ikhtilaf between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools: from which side should the deceased be placed into the grave? The Hanafi school relies on a direct hadith of the Prophet ﷺ, while the Shafi'i school follows the practice of a companion. Understanding this dispute clarifies how proof hierarchy works in Hanafi usul.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi ruling and its primary evidence
The matn says: 'and the deceased is entered from the side facing the qibla'. The evidence is the hadith of Ibn Abbas that the Prophet entered a grave from the qibla side.
This is an explicit action of the Prophet (fi'l), which is strong evidence.
2
Identify the Shafi'i position and its evidence
The Shafi'i school holds it is sunnah to enter from the feet side. Their evidence is the practice of the companion Al-Harith, reported by Abu Ishaq.
This is a statement of a tabi'i (successor), weaker than a direct hadith.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response to the Shafi'i proof
The Hanafi response is that the Prophet's action takes precedence over a companion's practice. The Shafi'i proof is a mursal report (a tabi'i narrating from a companion) and does not override a direct hadith.
In Hanafi usul, a hadith from the Prophet is qati' al-thubut when mutawatir, but here it is ahad, still stronger than a companion's practice.
4
Determine the practical consequence
The thamarah al-khilaf: Hanafis enter from the qibla side; Shafi'is from the feet side. Both are valid, but the mufta bihi in Hanafi is the qibla side.
Muslims should follow their respective madhhabs.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فَإِذَا بَلَغُوا إِلَى قَبْرِهِ كُرِهَ لِلنَّاسِ الْقُعُودُ قَبْلَ أَنْ يُوضَعَ عَنْ أَعْنَاقِ الرِّجَالِ وَيُحْفَرُ الْقَبْرُ وَيُلْحَدُ وَيُدْخَلُ الْمَيِّتُ مِمَّا يَلِي الْقِبْلَةَ

وجه (۱) قول الصحابي لثبوت فَإِذَا بَلَغُوا إِلَى قَبْرِهِ كُرِهَ لِلنَّاسِ الْقُعُودُ \ عَنْ أَبِي هُرَيْرَةَ، «أَنَّهُ لَمْ يَكُنْ يَقْعُدُ حَتَّى يُوضَعَ السَّرِيرُ» (مصنف ابن ابي شيبه فِي الرَّجُلِ يَكُونُ مَعَ الْجِنَازَةِ مَنْ قَالَ: لَا يجلس حَتَّى تُوضَعَ، نمبر 11510)

و وجه : (۱) قول الصحابي لثبوت وَيُحْفَرُ الْقَبْرُ وَيُلْحَدُ \ أن سعد بن أبي وقاص قَالَ فِي مَرَضِهِ الَّذِي هَلَكَ فِيهِ : الْخُدُوا لِي خَدًا وَانْصِبُوا عَلَيَّ اللَّبِنَ نَصْبًا . كَمَا صُنعَ بِرَسُولِ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم (مسلم شريف، بَاب فِي اللَّحْدِ وَنَصْبِ اللَّبِنَ عَلَى الْمَيِّتِ، نمبر 966)

وجه:(۲) الحديث لثبوت وَيُحْفَرُ الْقَبْرُ وَيُلْحَدُ عَنْ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ قَالَ: قَالَ النَّبِيُّ صلى الله عليه وسلم: «اللَّحْدُ لَنَا ، وَالشَّقُ لِغَيْرِنَا» (مسلم شريف ، بَابُ مَاجَاءَ فِي قَوْلِ النّبي الله اللَّحْدُ لَنَا، وَالشَّقُّ لِغَيْرِنَا، 1045)

وجه : (1) الحديث لثبوت وَيُدْخَلُ الْمَيِّتُ مِمَّا يَلِي الْقِبْلَةَ \ عَنْ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ، أَنَّ النَّبِيَّ صلى الله عليه وسلم دَخَلَ قَبْرًا لَيْلًا، فَأَسْرِجَ لَهُ سِرَاحٌ، فَأَخَذَهُ مِنْ قِبَلِ القِبْلَةِ، وَقَالَ: «رَحِمَكَ اللَّهُ، إِنْ كُنْتَ لَأَوَّاهًا تَلَّاءً لِلْقُرْآنِ»، وَكَبَّرَ عَلَيْهِ أَرْبَعًا» (سنن الترمذى، بَابُ مَا جَاءَ فِي الدَّفْنِ بِاللَّيْلِ،نمبر1057)

وجه:(1) دليل الشافعي قول التابعي لثبوت وَيُدْخَلُ الْمَيِّتُ مِمَّا يَلِي الْقِبْلَةَ \ عَنْ أَبِي إِسْحَاقَ، قَالَ: أَوْصَى الْحَارِثُ أَنْ يُصَلِّيَ عَلَيْهِ عَبْدُ اللَّهِ بْنُ يَزِيدَ، " فَصَلَّى عَلَيْهِ، ثُمَّ أَدْخَلَهُ الْقَبْرَ مِنْ قِبَلِ رِجْلَي الْقَبْرِ، وَقَالَ: هَذَا مِنَ السُّنَّةِ " (سنن ابوداود، بَابٌ فِي الْمَيِّتِ يُدْخَلُ مِنْ رِجْلَيْهِ، غبر 3211)

اصول: قبر کھودنے کے دو طریقے ہیں: (۱) لحد یعنی بغلی قبر، اور یہی مسنون طریقہ ہے۔ (۲) شق یعنی قبر کو سیدھا کھودا جائے، یہ طریقہ بھی جائز ہے جبکہ مٹی نرم ہو اور قبر بیٹھ جانے کا اندیشہ ہو۔
When they arrive at his grave, it is disliked for the people to sit before it is placed down from the necks of men, and the grave is dug and it is made a lahd, and the deceased is entered from the side facing the qibla. Evidence (1) statement of companion for proof of 'when they arrive...': from Abu Hurairah that he would not sit until the bier was placed. And evidence (1) statement of companion for proof of 'and the grave is dug and it is made a lahd': that Sa'd ibn Abi Waqqas said in his illness in which he died: 'Make a lahd for me and set up bricks over me standing, as was done with the Messenger of Allah.' Evidence (2) hadith for proof of 'and the grave is dug and it is made a lahd': from Ibn Abbas, the Prophet said: 'The lahd is for us, and the shaq is for others.' Evidence (1) hadith for proof of 'and the deceased is entered from the side facing the qibla': from Ibn Abbas that the Prophet entered a grave at night, a lamp was lit for him, so he took him from the direction of the qibla and said... Evidence (1) evidence of al-Shafi'i: statement of a tabi'i for proof of 'and the deceased is entered from the side facing the qibla': from Abu Ishaq, he said: Al-Harith willed that Abdullah ibn Yazid pray over him, so he prayed over him, then he entered him into the grave from the direction of the feet of the grave and said: 'This is from the sunnah.' Principle: there are two methods of digging the grave: (1) lahd, i.e., a side grave, and this is the sunnah method. (2) shaq, i.e., the grave is dug straight, this method is also permissible when the soil is soft and there is fear of the grave collapsing.
Source pages p. 182

Commentary
This passage from Al-Quduri's matn, with its accompanying hadith evidence, details the etiquettes upon arrival at the graveside. It begins by ruling that it is makruh (disliked) for people to sit down before the bier is lowered from the shoulders of the carriers. This is based on the practice of Abu Hurairah. Next, it states that the grave must be dug, and it should be a lahd (a niche dug into the side of the grave cavity) rather than a shaq (a straight trench). The Prophet's hadith explicitly says 'اللحد لنا والشق لغيرنا' (the lahd is for us, the shaq is for others), indicating that the lahd is the sunnah for Muslims. However, the Urdu note clarifies that if the soil is loose and there is a risk of collapse, a shaq is permissible. Finally, the passage stipulates that the deceased should be interred from the qibla side, meaning the body is inserted headfirst from the direction of the qibla. The Hanafi proof is the hadith of Ibn Abbas where the Prophet entered a grave from the qibla side. The Shafi'i school, however, considers it sunnah to enter from the feet side, based on the practice of the companion Al-Harith as reported by Abu Ishaq. The Hanafi response, though not explicitly rebutted here, is that the stronger evidence supports the qibla side, and the Shafi'i proof is a practice of a single companion that does not override the explicit action of the Prophet.

Key Terms
قِبَلِ الْقِبْلَةِ (qibal al-qiblah): The direction of the qibla; from the side facing the qibla.
رِجْلَي الْقَبْرِ (rijlay al-qabr): The feet side of the grave; the side where the feet of the deceased will be.
اللَّحْد (al-lahd): A niche dug into the side of the grave cavity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the main difference between Hanafi and Shafi'i positions on entering the deceased?
A) Hanafi: from qibla; Shafi'i: from feet
B) Hanafi: from feet; Shafi'i: from qibla
C) Both enter from qibla
D) Both enter from feet

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school enters the deceased from the qibla side based on the Prophet's action, overriding the Shafi'i proof from a companion's practice.

Rulings on Placing the Deceased in the Grave
Matn ruling with hadith proofs for specific actions during burial.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four recommended actions when placing the deceased in the grave and identify the hadith evidence for each.

Core Idea
Four sunan actions at burial: saying Bismillah, facing qibla, loosening knots, arranging bricks.

The deceased's placement in the grave is a pivotal moment marked by specific sunan actions. This lesson covers the four sunan derived from the Prophet's practice, as cited in the matn of Al-Quduri, each supported by hadith evidence. Understanding these as sunnah muakkadah ensures proper practice without overburdening.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four actions
Read the matn and list the four actions prescribed: saying the du'a, facing the qibla, loosening knots, arranging bricks.
The matn also includes the phrasing of the du'a.
2
Locate the hadith proof for each
For each action, identify the evidence provided in the shahr (commentary). Note the source and the type of evidence (hadith, companion statement, etc.).
3
Understand the legal level
From the Hanafi perspective, these actions are sunnah muakkadah. Determine what that means for validity and reward.
Omission does not invalidate the burial but is discouraged.
4
Analyze the evidence strength
Classify each evidence as marfu', mawquf, or maqtu'. Evaluate which proofs are strongest for establishing the sunnah.
The du'a and qibla have direct Prophet statements; knots and bricks rely on companion and successor practices.
5
Apply to a real burial
Consider how these actions are performed in a typical Hanafi burial today. Note any contemporary adjustments (e.g., using concrete slabs instead of bricks).
The sunnah is in the action, not the specific material.

فَإِذَا وُضِعَ فِي لَحْدِهِ قَالَ الَّذِي يَضَعُهُ بِاسْمِ اللَّهِ وَعَلَى مِلَّةِ رَسُولِ اللَّهِ وَيُوَجَّهُ إِلَى الْقِبْلَةِ وَتُحَلُّ الْعُقَدُ عَنْهُ وَيُسَوَّى اللَّبِنُ عَلَيْهِ

وجه : (۱) الحديث لثبوت فَإِذَا وُضِعَ فِي لَحَدِهِ قَالَ الَّذِي يَضَعُهُ \ عَنْ ابْنِ عُمَرَ، أَنَّ النَّبِيَّ صلى الله عليه وسلم كَانَ إِذَا أُدْخِلَ المَيْتُ القَبْرَ ، وَقَالَ أَبُو خَالِدٍ مَرَّةً : إِذَا وُضِعَ المَيْتُ فِي حَدِهِ، قَالَ مَرَّةً: «بِسْمِ اللَّهِ وَبِاللَّهِ، وَعَلَى مِلَّةِ رَسُولِ اللَّهِ»، وَقَالَ مَرَّةً: «بِسْمِ اللَّهِ وَبِاللَّهِ وَعَلَى سُنَّةِ رَسُولِ اللَّهِ » »(سنن الترمذى، بَابُ مَا يَقُولُ إِذَا أُدْخِلَ المَيْتُ القَبْرَ، نمبر 1046)

وجه : (۱) الحديث لثبوت وَيُوَجَّهُ إِلَى الْقِبْلَةِ \ أَنَّ رَجُلًا سَأَلَهُ، فَقَالَ: يَا رَسُولَ اللَّهِ مَا الْكَبَائِرُ؟ فَقَالَ: «هُنَّ تِسْعٌ»، فَذَكَرَ مَعْنَاهُ زَادَ: «وَعُقُوقُ الْوَالِدَيْنِ الْمُسْلِمَيْنِ، وَاسْتِحْلَالُ الْبَيْتِ الْحَرَامِ قِبْلَتِكُمْ أَحْيَاءً وَأَمْوَاتًا» (سنن ابوداود، بَابُ مَا جَاءَ فِي التَّشْدِيدِ فِي أَكْلِ مَالِ اليتيم، نمبر 2875/ السنن الكبري للبيهقي، بَابُ مَا جَاءَ فِي اسْتِقْبَالِ الْقِبْلَةِ بِالْمَوْتَى، نمبر 6724)

وجه:(۱) الحديث لثبوت وَتُحَلُّ الْعُقَدُ عَنْهُ عَنْ إِبْرَاهِيمَ، قَالَ: «إِذَا أُدْخِلَ الْمَيِّتُ الْقَبْرَ حُرَّ عَنْهُ الْعُقَدُ كُلُّهَا» (مصنف ابن ابي شيبه: مَا قَالُوا فِي حَلَ الْعُقَدَ عَنِ الْمَيِّتِ، نمبر 11669)

وجه : (۱) قول الصحابي لثبوت وَيُسَوَّى اللَّبِنُ عَلَيْهِ \ أن سعد بن أبي وقاص قَالَ فِي مَرَضِهِ الَّذِي هَلَكَ فِيهِ: الخُدُوا لِي لَخَدًا. وَانْصِبُوا عَلَيَّ اللَّبِنَ نَصْبًا. كَمَا صُنعَ بِرَسُولِ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم (مسلم شريف، بَاب فِي اللَّحْدِ وَنَصْبِ اللَّبِنَ عَلَى الْمَيِّتِ ، نمبر 966)

وجه (۲) الحديث لثبوت وَيُسَوَّى اللَّبِنُ عَلَيْهِ \ عَنْ عَلِيِّ بْنِ حُسَيْنٍ، «أَنَّهُمْ عَلَى قَبْرِ رَسُولِ اللَّهِ نَصَبُوا اللَّبِنَ نَصْبًا» (مصنف ابن ابي شيبه في اللَّبِنِ يُنْتَصَبُ عَلَى الْقَبْرِ أَوْ يُبْنَى بِنَاء، نمبر 11730)

اصول : میت کا رُخ قبلہ کی طرف کر کے کفن کی گرہیں کھول دینا مسنون ہے۔
When he is placed in his lahd, the one who places him says: 'In the name of Allah and upon the religion of the Messenger of Allah,' and he is turned to face the qibla, and the knots are loosened from him, and the bricks are arranged over him. Evidence (1) hadith for proof of 'when he is placed in his lahd, the one who places him says...': from Ibn Umar that the Prophet, when the deceased was entered into the grave, once said: 'Bismillah wa billah, wa ala millati Rasulillah' and another time: 'Bismillah wa billah wa ala sunnati Rasulillah'. Evidence (1) hadith for proof of 'and he is turned to face the qibla': that a man asked the Prophet about major sins, and he mentioned nine, and added: 'and disobedience to Muslim parents, and violating the sanctity of the Sacred House, your qibla, alive and dead.' Evidence (1) hadith for proof of 'and the knots are loosened from him': from Ibrahim, he said: 'When the deceased is entered into the grave, all knots are loosened from him.' Evidence (1) statement of companion for proof of 'and the bricks are arranged over him': that Sa'd ibn Abi Waqqas said in his illness in which he died: 'Make a lahd for me and set up bricks over me standing, as was done with the Messenger of Allah.' Evidence (2) hadith for proof of 'and the bricks are arranged over him': from Ali ibn Husayn: 'They set up bricks over the grave of the Messenger of Allah standing.' Principle: It is sunnah to turn the deceased to face the qibla and to undo the knots of the shroud.
Source pages p. 183

Commentary
This passage continues the burial instructions from the matn of Al-Quduri, detailing the actions when placing the deceased into the lahd. It prescribes that the person placing the body should say 'بسم الله وعلى ملة رسول الله' (In the name of Allah and upon the religion of the Messenger of Allah). The evidence from Ibn Umar shows the Prophet used variations of this phrase. Then the deceased should be turned to face the qibla. The hadith about major sins includes the statement that the Ka'ba is the qibla of Muslims both alive and dead, indicating respect for the qibla direction. Next, the knots of the shroud should be loosened. The report from Ibrahim states that all knots are untied when the deceased is placed in the grave. Finally, bricks (or unfired mud blocks) are arranged over the lahd to seal it, as was done for the Prophet. The Urdu note summarizes that it is sunnah to turn the deceased to face the qibla and to undo the knots. All of these actions are considered mustahabb (recommended) in the Hanafi school, not obligatory.

Key Terms
الْعُقَد (al-ʿuqad): The knots of the shroud (kafan) that are untied after placing the deceased in the grave.
اللَّبِن (al-labin): Unbaked bricks or mud blocks used to cover the lahd and seal the grave.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on loosening the knots of the shroud when placing the deceased in the grave?
A) It is wajib
B) It is sunnah
C) It is mubah
D) It is makruh

Key Takeaway
The four actions when placing the deceased in the grave are strongly recommended sunan muakkadah, each supported by authentic hadith or practice of the Companions.

Sunnan of Burial: Placing, Facing Qibla, Undoing Knots, Leveling Bricks
Matn with hadith proofs for sunnah acts at burial

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four sunnah acts to be performed when placing the deceased in the grave and identify the hadith evidence for each.

Core Idea
Four sunnah acts at burial: saying Bismillah, facing qibla, undoing knots, leveling bricks.

When the deceased is placed in the grave, certain actions are sunnah muakkadah based on the practice of the Prophet ﷺ and the Companions. This lesson presents the four recommended acts from the matn of Al-Quduri, along with their hadith proofs.

Guided Path
1
Identify each sunnah act
Read the matn and list the four actions: saying the du'a, turning the deceased to face the qibla, undoing the knots of the shroud, and leveling bricks over the lahd.
The matn uses 'wa' (and) to connect them.
2
Locate the hadith evidence
For each action, the matn or commentary provides a hadith. Match each action to its primary evidence: du'a (Ibn Umar hadith), qibla (Bayhaqi hadith), undoing knots (Ibn Abi Shaybah report from Ibrahim al-Nakha'i), bricks (Muslim hadith of Sa'd ibn Abi Waqqas).
3
Understand the legal weight
Note that all four actions are classified as sunnah muakkadah (emphasized sunnah), not wajib. This is because the evidence (ahad hadith) is zanni in transmission and meaning, and the imperative form is understood as recommendation.
The Hanafi position is that omitting any of these does not invalidate the burial but loses reward.
4
Note any ikhtilaf
Some Shafi'i scholars may consider facing the qibla as mustahabb with a different method of entering the grave; however, the Hanafi view is that it is sunnah muakkadah.

فَإِذَا وُضِعَ فِي خَدِهِ قَالَ الَّذِي يَضَعُهُ بِاسْمِ اللَّهِ وَعَلَى مِلَّةِ رَسُولِ اللَّهِ ١٣ وَيُوَجَّهُ إِلَى الْقِبْلَةِ ١٣ وَتُحَلُّ الْعُقَدُ عَنْهُ ١٤ وَيُسَوَّى اللَّبِنُ عَلَيْهِ
لِلْقُرْآنِ»، وَكَبَّرَ عَلَيْهِ أَرْبَعًا» (سنن الترمذى، بَابُ مَا جَاءَ فِي الدَّفْنِ بِاللَّيْلِ،نمبر1057) وجه:(1) دليل الشافعي قول التابعي لثبوت وَيُدْخَلُ الْمَيِّتُ مِمَّا يَلِي الْقِبْلَةَ \ عَنْ أَبِي إِسْحَاقَ، قَالَ: أَوْصَى الْحَارِثُ أَنْ يُصَلِّيَ عَلَيْهِ عَبْدُ اللَّهِ بْنُ يَزِيدَ، " فَصَلَّى عَلَيْهِ، ثُمَّ أَدْخَلَهُ الْقَبْرَ مِنْ قِبَلِ رِجْلَي الْقَبْرِ، وَقَالَ: هَذَا مِنَ السُّنَّةِ " (سنن ابوداود، بَابٌ فِي الْمَيِّتِ يُدْخَلُ مِنْ رِجْلَيْهِ، غبر 3211) ال وجه : (۱) الحديث لثبوت فَإِذَا وُضِعَ فِي لَحَدِهِ قَالَ الَّذِي يَضَعُهُ \ عَنْ ابْنِ عُمَرَ، أَنَّ النَّبِيَّ صلى الله عليه وسلم كَانَ إِذَا أُدْخِلَ المَيْتُ القَبْرَ ، وَقَالَ أَبُو خَالِدٍ مَرَّةً : إِذَا وُضِعَ المَيْتُ فِي حَدِهِ، قَالَ مَرَّةً: «بِسْمِ اللَّهِ وَبِاللَّهِ، وَعَلَى مِلَّةِ رَسُولِ اللَّهِ»، وَقَالَ مَرَّةً: «بِسْمِ اللَّهِ وَبِاللَّهِ وَعَلَى سُنَّةِ رَسُولِ اللَّهِ » »(سنن الترمذى، بَابُ مَا يَقُولُ إِذَا أُدْخِلَ المَيْتُ القَبْرَ، نمبر 1046)
وجه : (۱) الحديث لثبوت وَيُوَجَّهُ إِلَى الْقِبْلَةِ \ أَنَّ رَجُلًا سَأَلَهُ، فَقَالَ: يَا رَسُولَ اللَّهِ مَا الْكَبَائِرُ؟ فَقَالَ: «هُنَّ تِسْعٌ» (سنن ابوداود، بَابُ مَا جَاءَ فِي التَّشْدِيدِ فِي أَكْلِ مَالِ اليتيم، نمبر 2875) زَادَ: «وَعُقُوقُ الْوَالِدَيْنِ الْمُسْلِمَيْنِ، وَاسْتِحْلَالُ الْبَيْتِ الْحَرَامِ قِبْلَتِكُمْ أَحْيَاء وَأَمْوَاتًا» (السنن الكبري للبيهقي، بَابُ مَا جَاءَ فِي اسْتِقْبَالِ الْقِبْلَةِ بِالْمَوْتَى، نمبر 6724) وجه:(۱) الحديث لثبوت وَتُحَلُّ الْعُقَدُ عَنْهُ عَنْ إِبْرَاهِيمَ، قَالَ: «إِذَا أُدْخِلَ الْمَيِّتُ الْقَبْرَ حُرَّ عَنْهُ الْعُقَدُ كُلُّهَا» (مصنف ابن ابي شيبه: مَا قَالُوا فِي حَلَ الْعُقَدَ عَنِ الْمَيِّتِ، نمبر 11669) وجه : (۱) قول الصحابي لثبوت وَيُسَوَّى اللَّبِنُ عَلَيْهِ \ أن سعد بن أبي وقاص قَالَ فِي مَرَضِهِ الَّذِي هَلَكَ فِيهِ: الخَدُوا لِي لَخَدًا. وَانْصِبُوا عَلَيَّ اللَّبِنَ نَصْبًا. كَمَا صُنعَ بِرَسُولِ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم (مسلم شريف، بَاب فِي اللَّحْدِ وَنَصْبِ اللَّبِنَ عَلَى الْمَيِّتِ ، نمبر 966)
وجه (۲) الحديث لثبوت وَيُسَوَّى اللَّبِنُ عَلَيْهِ \ عَنْ عَلِيِّ بْنِ حُسَيْنٍ، «أَنَّهُمْ عَلَى قَبْرِ رَسُولِ اللَّهِ نَصَبُوا اللَّبِنَ نَصْبَّا» (مصنف ابن ابي شيبه في اللَّبِنِ يُنْتَصَبُ عَلَى الْقَبْرِ أَوْ يُبْنَى بِنَاء، نمبر 11730)
اصول : میت کا رُخ قبلہ کی طرف کر کے کفن کی گرہیں کھول دینا مسنون ہے۔
When he is placed in his grave, the one who places him says: 'In the name of Allah and upon the religion of the Messenger of Allah'. And he is turned to face the qibla. And the knots are undone from him. And the bricks are leveled over him. ... Evidence for facing qibla: A man asked the Prophet about major sins, and he mentioned nine, including 'making lawful the Sacred House, your qibla, alive and dead'. ... Principle: It is sunnah to turn the deceased towards the qibla and to undo the knots of the shroud.
Source pages p. 183

Commentary
This passage presents the sunnah acts to be performed when placing the deceased in the grave. The person placing the body says 'Bismillah wa 'ala millati Rasoolillah' as narrated in hadith. The deceased is turned to face the qibla based on the hadith where the Prophet mentioned the Ka'bah as the qibla for both the living and the dead. The Hanafi position is that facing qibla is sunnah, not obligatory. The knots of the shroud are undone, as reported from Ibrahim al-Nakha'i. Finally, bricks are placed over the grave, following the practice of Sa'd ibn Abi Waqqas and the Prophet's own grave. The Urdu usul confirms these actions as masnun (recommended).

Key Terms
اللَّحْد (al-lahd): A niche dug into the side of the grave to place the body, as opposed to a shaqq (a trench).
اللَّبِن (al-labin): Unbaked bricks made of mud and straw, used to cover the lahd.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on undoing the knots of the shroud after placing the deceased in the grave?
A) Wajib
B) Sunnah
C) Mubah
D) Haram

Key Takeaway
The four sunnah acts at burial are rooted in prophetic practice and are recommended, not obligatory.

Grave Covering Materials: Makruh vs Mubah
Ruling on grave covering materials with proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on grave covering materials and apply it to distinguish between permanent and temporary materials.

Core Idea
Permanent grave construction is makruh; natural materials that decay are permissible.

This lesson examines a ruling from Al-Quduri on what materials may be used to cover a grave. The matn declares baked bricks (ajurr) and wood (khashab) as makruh, while reeds (qasab) are without harm. The proof is drawn from a hadith prohibiting building over graves and from the practice of the early Muslims. Understanding this distinction helps maintain the simplicity of grave markers in accordance with Sunnah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling on each material
From the matn: baked bricks (ajurr) and wood (khashab) are makruh; reeds (qasab) are mubah (no harm). Note the level: makruh tanzihi (mildly disliked).
The Urdu commentary clarifies that any permanent firming of the grave is makruh.
2
Locate the dalil (evidence)
The author cites two evidences: (1) the hadith of Jabir in which the Prophet forbade building over graves (al-bina'), and (2) the statement of Ibrahim al-Nakha'i that they preferred unbaked bricks (labin) and reeds and disliked baked bricks and wood.
The hadith is from Sahih Muslim and Sunan Abi Dawud.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah (legal implication)
The prohibition of building over graves is general (amm) and includes any permanent structure. Baked bricks and wood create a lasting edifice, resembling habitations, thus makruh. Reeds are not permanent and therefore not included in the prohibition.
The Hanafi principle: al-amm yufidu al-tahrim, but here the ruling is makruh due to the nature of the material.
4
Note the exception and its basis
Reeds (qasab) are explicitly excluded. Also, unbaked bricks (labin) are considered permissible or preferred (from Ibrahim's statement). The basis is the practice of the Salaf and the temporary nature of these materials.
This shows the Hanafi distinction between permanent and temporary construction.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَيُكْرَهُ الآجُرُّ وَالْخَشَبُ وَلا بَأْسَ بِالْقَصَبِ ١٦
وجه: (1) الحديث لثبوت وَيُكْرَهُ الْآجُرُّ وَالْخَشَبُ وَلَا بَأْسَ بِالْقَصَبِ \ عَنْ جَابِرٍ؛ قَالَ: نَهَى رَسُولُ اللهِ أَنْ يُخصَّصَ الْقَبْرُ. وَأَنْ يُقْعَدَ عَلَيْهِ. وَأَنْ يُبْنَى عَلَيْهِ، (مسلم شريف : بَاب النَّهْي عَنْ تخصيص الْقَبْرِ وَالْبِنَاءِ عَلَيْهِ، نمبر 970/سنن ابوداود ، بَابٌ فِي الْبِنَاءِ عَلَى الْقَبْرِ ، نمبر 3225 وجه : (۲) قول التابعي لثبوت وَيُكْرَهُ الْآجُرُّ وَالْخَشَبُ وَلَا بَأْسَ بِالْقَصَبِ \ عَنْ إِبْرَاهِيمَ، قَالَ: «كَانُوا يَسْتَحِبُّونَ اللَّبِنَ، وَيَكْرَهُونَ الآجُرَّ، وَيَسْتَحِبُّونَ الْقَصَبَ، وَيَكْرَهُونَ الْخَشَبَ» (مصنف ابن ابي شيبه في تَجْصِيص الْقَبْرِ وَالْآجُرّ يُجْعَلُ لَهُ، غير 11770)
اصول: قبر کو پکی کر ناخواہ پکی اینٹ سے ہو یا پھر مضبوط لکڑی سے، مکروہ ہے۔
And baked bricks and wood are disliked, but there is no harm in reeds. ... Evidence: Jabir said the Prophet forbade plastering graves, sitting on them, and building over them. ... From Ibrahim: 'They used to prefer unbaked bricks and dislike baked bricks, and prefer reeds and dislike wood.' Principle: Making a grave firm, whether with baked bricks or strong wood, is makrooh.
Source pages p. 184

Commentary
This ruling addresses the materials used in grave construction. The matn states that using baked bricks (ajurr) and wood (khashab) is makruh, while reeds (qasab) are permissible. The proof comes from the hadith of Jabir where the Prophet prohibited building over graves, which includes using permanent materials. Ibrahim al-Nakha'i's statement confirms the preference for unbaked bricks (labin) and reeds. The Urdu usul clarifies that making the grave firm with baked bricks or wood is disliked; this includes any permanent construction. The Hanafi school views this as makruh tanzihi (mildly disliked).

Key Terms
الآجُرُّ (al-ajurr): Baked bricks, often kiln-fired, used for construction.
الْقَصَبُ (al-qasab): Reeds or bamboo, a natural material that does not last; permissible.
الْخَشَبُ (al-khashab): Wood, especially when used in permanent construction.
اللَّبِنُ (al-labin): Unbaked bricks (mud bricks), preferred by Salaf.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which material for covering a grave is considered makruh?
A) Unbaked bricks (labin)
B) Reeds (qasab)
C) Baked bricks (ajurr)
D) Soil

Key Takeaway
Permanent grave covers are makruh tanzihi; only temporary natural materials like reeds are permissible.

The Sunnah of Shaping the Grave: Musannam vs. Musattah
Ruling on how to shape the grave: heap earth and raise it like a camel hump

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on grave shape (musannam) and reconcile the apparent conflict between the hadith of tasnim and the hadith of leveling.

Core Idea
The grave should be raised like a camel hump (musannam), not flat.

The Prophet's grave was observed to be musannam, and the command to level graves applies to excessive elevation. This lesson examines the dalil and the Hanafi position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling statement
Read the Arabic matn: 'ثُمَّ يُهَالُ التَّرَابُ عَلَيْهِ وَيُسَنَّمُ الْقَبْرُ وَلَا يُسَطَّحُ'. What is the explicit ruling?
The phrase 'وَيُسَنَّمُ' commands tasnim; 'وَلَا يُسَطَّحُ' prohibits tasth.
2
Examine the first dalil (tasnim)
Consider the hadith of Sufyan al-Tammar seeing the Prophet's grave musannam. How does this directly support the ruling?
Direct observation of the Prophet's practice establishes sunnah.
3
Examine the second dalil (leveling)
Read the hadith from Muslim: the Prophet sent Ali to level every raised grave. How does this not contradict the first hadith?
Hanafis interpret 'raised' (mushrif) as excessively high, not the normal slight elevation.
4
Reconcile the two dala'il
Combine both: the sunnah is to make the grave slightly raised like a hump, but not excessively. This reconciles both proofs.
The matn's instruction to not make it flat (la yusattah) aligns with the tasnim hadith.
5
State the final Hanafi position
Conclude: tasnim is sunnah muakkadah, tasth is makruh. This is the mufta bihi.
The Urdu usul confirms: 'قبر کو مٹی سے کوہان نما بنائی جائے بالکل چوکور نہ بنائی جائے'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثُمَّ يُهَالُ التَّرَابُ عَلَيْهِ وَيُسَنَّمُ الْقَبْرُ وَلَا يُسَطَّحُ ك
وجه: (1) الحديث لثبوت ثُمَّ يُهَالُ التُّرَابُ عَلَيْهِ وَيُسَنَّمُ الْقَبْرُ \ عَنْ سُفْيَانَ التَّمَّارِ أَنَّهُ حَدَّثَهُ: «أَنَّهُ رَأَى قَبْرَ النَّبِيِّ صلى الله عليه وسلم مُسَنَّمًا.» (صحيح البخاري: بَابُ مَا جَاءَ فِي قَبْرِ النَّبِيِّ صلى الله عليه وسلم وَأَبِي بَكْرٍ الله عنهما، نمبر 1390/مصنف ابن ابي شيبه، مَا قَالُوا فِي الْقَبْرِ يُسَنَّمُ، نمبر 11733) وجه:(۲) الحديث لثبوت ثُمَّ يُهَالُ التُّرَابُ عَلَيْهِ وَيُسَنَّمُ الْقَبْرُ \ قَالَ لِي عَلِيُّ بْنُ أَبِي طَالِبٍ: أَلَا أَبْعَثُكَ عَلَى مَا بَعَثَنِي عَلَيْهِ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ ؟ أَنْ لَا تَدَعَ تِمْثَالًا إِلَّا طَمَسْتَهُ. وَلَا قَبْرًا مُشْرِفًا إِلَّا سَوَّيْتَهُ (مسلم شريف، بَاب الْأَمْرِ بِتَسْوِيَةِ الْقَبْرِ، نمبر 969)
اصول : قبر کو مٹی سے کو ہان نما بنائی جائے بالکل چوکور نہ بنائی جائے، یہی مسنون ہے۔
Then earth is heaped over him, and the grave is made musannam (raised like a camel hump), and it is not made flat. ... Evidence: Sufyan al-Tammar said he saw the Prophet's grave as musannam. And Ali ibn Abi Talib said the Prophet sent him to level every raised grave. ... Principle: The grave should be made like a camel hump from earth, not completely square; this is the sunnah.
Source pages p. 184

Commentary
After burial, soil is poured over the grave and it is shaped into a raised form called 'musannam' (like a camel's hump). The matn explicitly says not to make it flat (musattah). The proof comes from the sighting of the Prophet's grave as musannam, narrated by Sufyan al-Tammar. The hadith of Ali about leveling elevated graves applies to those that are excessively raised, not the normal sunnah elevation. The Urdu usul confirms that making it like a camel hump is sunnah, and it should not be made completely square or flat. This is the Hanafi practice.

Key Terms
التَّسْنِيم (al-tasnim): The act of making the grave raised like a camel's hump, about a handspan high.
التَّسْطِيح (al-tasth): Making the grave flat, level with the ground.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the recommended shape of the grave in the Hanafi school?
A) Flat (musattah)
B) Raised like a camel hump (musannam)
C) Square (murabba')
D) No specific shape

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school rules that graves should be made musannam (raised like a camel hump) and not flat, based on the practice of the Prophet, reconciling the command to level graves as applying only to excessive elevation.

Janazah for Infants: Crying as the Sign of Life
Distinction between live-born and stillborn in janazah rulings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi criterion (istihlal) for an infant to receive the funeral prayer and identify the hadith proof.

Core Idea
A live-born infant (who cries) is given full janazah; a stillborn is wrapped and buried without prayer.

In Hanafi fiqh, not every deceased infant receives the funeral prayer. The key distinction is whether the infant showed a sign of life after birth, specifically crying (istihlal). This lesson explains the ruling and the prophetic evidence behind it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two cases
The matn presents two scenarios: an infant who cries after birth and one who does not. Recognize that the ruling for each is different.
Crying is the primary sign; other movements may be considered by other schools.
2
State the ruling for each case
For the infant who cries: named, washed, and prayed over (wajib). For the one who does not: wrapped in a cloth and buried without prayer.
The prayer is wajib when life is confirmed.
3
Locate the dalil
The author cites two hadith: 'The child is prayed over' and 'When the infant cries, he is prayed over and inherits.' Understand that these ahadith provide the legislative basis.
Both are from Sunan al-Nasa'i, grade: hasan.
4
Analyse the wajh al-dalalah
The first hadith is general; the second specifies that crying triggers the prayer. The conjunctive 'wa' in 'idha istahalla… salli 'alayh' links crying to the obligation.
Hanafi usul: amm makhsus – the general is specified by the condition.
5
Note the cross-madhhab nuance
Most schools agree that any sign of life (movement, sneeze) suffices, but Hanafis require a clear cry because it is the most reliable indicator.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf in evidentiary weight.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَمَنْ اسْتَهَلَّ بَعْدَ الْوِلَادَةِ سُمِّيَ وَغُسَلَ وَصُلِّيَ عَلَيْهِ وَإِنْ لَمْ يَسْتَهِنَّ أُدْرجَ فِي خِرْقَةٍ وَلَمْ يُصَلَّ عَلَيْهِ
وجه: (1) الحديث لثبوت وَمَنْ اسْتَهَلَّ بَعْدَ الْوِلَادَةِ سُمِّيَ \ عَنِ الْمُغِيرَةِ بْن شُعْبَةَ أَنَّهُ ذَكَرَ أَنَّ رَسُولَ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم قَالَ: «الرَّاكِبُ خَلْفَ الْجِنَازَةِ، وَالْمَاشِي حَيْثُ شَاءَ مِنْهَا، وَالطِّفْلُ يُصَلَّى عَلَيْهِ» (سنن نسائي، الصَّلَاةُ عَلَى الْأَطْفَالِ،،نمبر 1548)
وجه:(۲) الحديث لثبوت وَمَنْ اسْتَهَلَّ بَعْدَ الْوِلَادَةِ سُمِّيَ \ عَنْ جَابِرِ بْنِ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ، قَالَ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم: «إِذَا اسْتَهَلَّ الصَّبِيُّ، صُلِّيَ عَلَيْهِ وَوُرِثَ» (سنن نسائي، بَابُ مَا جَاءَ فِي الصَّلَاةِ عَلَى الطَّفْل،،نمبر 1508)
And whoever cries after birth is named, washed, and prayed over. If he does not cry, he is wrapped in a piece of cloth and no prayer is offered over him. ... Evidence: The Prophet said 'The child is prayed over' and 'When the infant cries, he is prayed over and inherits.'
Source pages p. 184

Commentary
This passage distinguishes between a live-born infant (one who cries or shows any sign of life) and a stillbirth. If the infant cries (istahalla) after birth, it is considered a living human being entitled to full janazah rites: naming, ghusl, and funeral prayer. The proofs come from hadith where the Prophet stated that a child who cries is prayed over and inherits. If there is no cry (or other sign of life), the infant is simply wrapped in a cloth and buried without prayer, as it is not considered a person with a soul that separated. The Hanafi school follows this ruling: the criterion is istihlal (crying) or any equivalent sign of life.

Key Terms
اسْتَهَلَّ (istahalla): To cry or shout at birth, indicating the infant is alive.
الخِرْقَة (al-khirqah): A piece of cloth used to wrap a stillborn infant.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the criterion for an infant to receive the funeral prayer (salah al-janazah) in the Hanafi school?
A) The infant must be full-term
B) The infant must cry after birth
C) The parents request it
D) The infant must be named

Key Takeaway
An infant who cries after birth is given full janazah; a stillborn is wrapped and buried without prayer.

Grave Building Materials: Baked Brick, Wood, and Reeds
Ruling on grave materials with ḥadīth and Successor proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on using baked bricks, wood, and reeds for grave construction and explain the evidence from hadith and practice of the Salaf.

Core Idea
Baked bricks and wood are disliked for graves; reeds are permissible — the prohibition is makruh tanzihi, not haram.

This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling on what materials may be used to build or cover a grave. The matn of al-Quduri states that baked brick (ājurr) and wood are makruh, while reeds (qaṣab) are permissible. The author supports this with a hadith prohibiting building over graves and a report from the Successor Ibrāhīm al-Nakha‘ī, showing the practice of the early Muslims.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is using baked brick (ājurr) or wood to construct a grave. The ruling is makruh (disliked). The text also states that reeds (qaṣab) are permissible (lā ba’s).
Makruh here is tanzihi (not sinful but better avoided).
2
Locate the primary dalil
The first proof is the hadith from Jābir ibn ‘Abdillāh: the Prophet ﷺ forbade plastering the grave, sitting on it, and building over it. The term ‘building over it’ (an yubnā ‘alayhi) includes using permanent materials like brick and wood.
Hadith narrated by Muslim (no. 970) and Abū Dāwūd (no. 3225).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalālah
The prohibition (nahy) in the hadith indicates karāhah (dislike) according to Hanafi uṣūl, not taḥrīm, because the context allows exceptions (e.g., necessity). The permissibility of reeds is derived from the positive practice of the Salaf.
The second proof is the statement of Ibrāhīm al-Nakha‘ī that they used to prefer unbaked brick and reeds, dislike baked brick and wood.
4
Note the ikhtilāf
Some Shāfi‘ī and Mālikī scholars permit baked brick if not excessive, but the Ḥanafī school maintains karāhah based on the generality of the prohibition.
The difference is one of interpretation of the prohibition's strength.
5
Evaluate the tarjīḥ
The Ḥanafī position is from the ẓāhir al-riwāyah as recorded by al-Qudurī, and it is the muftā bihī view.
No intra-Ḥanafī disagreement on this ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَيُكْرَهُ الْآجُرُّ وَالْخَشَبُ وَلا بَأْسَ بِالْقَصَبِ ثُمَّ يُهَالُ التُّرَابُ عَلَيْهِ وَيُسَنَّمُ الْقَبْرُ وَلَا يُسَطَّحُ

وجه: (1) الحديث لثبوت وَيُكْرَهُ الْآجُرُّ وَالْخَشَبُ وَلَا بَأْسَ بِالْقَصَبِ
عَنْ جَابِرٍ؛ قَالَ: نَهَى رَسُولُ اللهِ أَنْ يُخصَّصَ الْقَبْرُ. وَأَنْ يُقْعَدَ عَلَيْهِ. وَأَنْ يُبْنَى عَلَيْهِ، (مسلم شريف : بَاب النَّهْي عَنْ تخصيص الْقَبْرِ وَالْبِنَاءِ عَلَيْهِ، نمبر 970/سنن ابوداود ، بَابٌ فِي الْبِنَاءِ عَلَى الْقَبْرِ ، نمبر 3225)
وجه : (۲) قول التابعي لثبوت وَيُكْرَهُ الْآجُرُّ وَالْخَشَبُ وَلَا بَأْسَ بِالْقَصَبِ
عَنْ إِبْرَاهِيمَ، قَالَ: «كَانُوا يَسْتَحِبُّونَ اللَّبِنَ، وَيَكْرَهُونَ الآجُرَّ، وَيَسْتَحِبُّونَ الْقَصَبَ، وَيَكْرَهُونَ الْخَشَبَ» (مصنف ابن ابي شيبه في تَجْصِيص الْقَبْرِ وَالْآجُرّ يُجْعَلُ لَهُ، غير 11770)
وجه : (1) الحديث لثبوت ثُمَّ يُهَالُ التُّرَابُ عَلَيْهِ وَيُسَنَّمُ الْقَبْرُ
عَنْ سُفْيَانَ التَّمَّارِ أَنَّهُ حَدَّثَهُ: «أَنَّهُ رَأَى قَبْرَ النَّبِيِّ صلى الله عليه وسلم مُسَنَّمًا.» (صحيح البخاري: بَابُ مَا جَاءَ فِي قَبْرِ النَّبِيِّ صلى الله عليه وسلم وَأَبِي بَكْرٍ الله عنهما، نمبر 1390/مصنف ابن ابي شيبه، مَا قَالُوا فِي الْقَبْرِ يُسَنَّمُ، نمبر 11733)
وجه:(۲) الحديث لثبوت ثُمَّ يُهَالُ التُّرَابُ عَلَيْهِ وَيُسَنَّمُ الْقَبْرُ
قَالَ لِي عَلِيُّ بْنُ أَبِي طَالِبٍ: أَلَا أَبْعَثُكَ عَلَى مَا بَعَثَنِي عَلَيْهِ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ ؟ أَنْ لَا تَدَعَ تِمْثَالًا إِلَّا طَمَسْتَهُ. وَلَا قَبْرًا مُشْرِفًا إِلَّا سَوَّيْتَهُ (مسلم شريف، بَاب الْأَمْرِ بِتَسْوِيَةِ الْقَبْرِ، نمبر 969)

قبر کو پکی کر ناخواہ پکی اینٹ سے ہو یا پھر مضبوط لکڑی سے، مکروہ ہے۔ اصول : قبر کو مٹی سے کو ہان نما بنائی جائے بالکل چوکور نہ بنائی جائے، یہی مسنون ہے۔
Baked brick and wood are disliked, and there is no harm in reeds. Then soil is poured over it and the grave is made hump-shaped and not flattened.

Proof (1): Hadith for 'Baked brick and wood are disliked, and there is no harm in reeds': From Jabir, he said: The Messenger of Allah forbade that a grave be plastered, that one sit on it, or that one build over it. (Muslim, Chapter: Prohibition of Plastering and Building over Graves, no. 970; Abu Dawud, Chapter: Building over Graves, no. 3225)
Proof (2): Statement of a Successor for 'Baked brick and wood are disliked, and there is no harm in reeds': From Ibrahim, he said: They used to prefer unbaked brick and dislike baked brick, and they used to prefer reeds and dislike wood. (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, regarding plastering the grave and using baked brick, no. 11770)
Proof (1): Hadith for 'Then soil is poured over it and the grave is made hump-shaped': From Sufyan al-Tammar that he narrated: He saw the grave of the Prophet (peace be upon him) hump-shaped. (Sahih al-Bukhari, Chapter: What has come about the grave of the Prophet and Abu Bakr, no. 1390; Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, What they said about the grave being hump-shaped, no. 11733)
Proof (2): Hadith for 'Then soil is poured over it and the grave is made hump-shaped': Ali ibn Abi Talib said to me: Shall I not send you on the same mission that the Messenger of Allah sent me? Do not leave any image without effacing it, nor any raised grave without levelling it. (Muslim, Chapter: Command to Level Graves, no. 969)

Principle: Making a grave hard – whether with baked brick or strong wood – is disliked. Principle: The grave should be made hump-shaped with soil, not completely square; that is the Sunnah.
Source pages p. 184

Commentary
This passage covers two related rulings on graves. The first ruling states that using baked bricks (ājurr) or wood for constructing graves is makrūh (disliked), but using reeds (qaṣab) is permissible. The textual operation is expansion_probe: the commentator brings two proofs—a hadith from Jabir forbidding plastering and building over graves, and a statement from the Successor Ibrahim al-Nakha'i reporting the practice of the early Muslims. The second ruling states that after burial, soil should be poured over the grave and it should be made musannam (hump-shaped, like a camel's hump), not musaṭṭaḥ (flattened). Two proofs are provided: the sighting of the Prophet's grave as musannam by Sufyan al-Tammar, and the hadith of Ali ibn Abi Talib recording the Prophet's command to level raised graves. The Urdu summary at the end reiterates that hardening the grave with baked brick or wood is disliked, and that the hump-shaped form is the Sunnah.

Key Terms
آجُرّ (ājurr): Baked brick, used in construction
قَصَب (qaṣab): Reed, a plant material

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It is haram and invalidates the burial.
B) It is makruh (disliked), but the burial is valid.
C) It is sunnah to use baked bricks.
D) It is wajib to avoid baked bricks.

Key Takeaway
Using baked brick or wood for a grave is makruh tanzihi; reeds are permissible.

Grave Shape: Hump-Shaped (Musannam) vs. Flattened (Musatṭaḥ)
Ruling on grave shape with ḥadīth proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school considers the hump-shaped grave (tasnīm) as sunnah and flattening (tasṭīḥ) as makruh, citing the relevant hadith proofs.

Core Idea
The grave should be made hump-shaped like a camel's hump; flattening it is not the Sunnah.

After burial, the grave should be shaped in a specific manner. The matn of al-Quduri states that soil is poured over the grave and it is made musannam (hump-shaped), not musaṭṭaḥ (flattened). The author provides two proofs: the sighting of the Prophet’s grave as hump-shaped and the command to level raised graves, which implies that the hump should be moderate.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is shaping the grave after burial. The text commands that it be made hump-shaped (musannam) and not flattened. This is a sunnah (recommended practice).
Tasnīm means raising the grave about one handspan high in the middle, like a camel's hump.
2
Locate the primary dalil
The first proof is the hadith from Sufyān al-Tammār: he saw the grave of the Prophet ﷺ as musannam (hump-shaped). The second proof is the hadith of ‘Alī ibn Abī Ṭālib: the Prophet ﷺ commanded him to level every raised grave (qabr mushrif).
Bukhari no. 1390; Muslim no. 969.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalālah
The sighting of the Prophet’s grave shows that the hump shape is the established practice (amal). The command to level raised graves indicates that graves should not be excessively high, but a moderate hump is not considered 'raised' in a prohibited sense.
The hump shape is a mean between being completely flat and excessively high.
4
Note the ikhtilāf
Some schools (e.g., Shāfi‘ī) consider flattening (tasṭīḥ) as sunnah, citing other hadith. The Ḥanafī school follows the practice of the Prophet’s grave.
Both views have evidence; the difference is over which practice is more authentic.
5
Evaluate the tarjīḥ
The Ḥanafī position is based on the direct observation of the Prophet’s grave and the general command to level only raised graves, which does not forbid a moderate hump.
This is the muftā bihī view in the Ḥanafī school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

عَنْ إِبْرَاهِيمَ، قَالَ: «كَانُوا يَسْتَحِبُّونَ اللَّبِنَ، وَيَكْرَهُونَ الآجُرَّ، وَيَسْتَحِبُّونَ الْقَصَبَ، وَيَكْرَهُونَ الْخَشَبَ» (مصنف ابن ابي شيبه في تَجْصِيص الْقَبْرِ وَالْآجُرّ يُجْعَلُ لَهُ، غير 11770)

وجه:(۲) الحديث لثبوت ثُمَّ يُهَالُ التُّرَابُ عَلَيْهِ وَيُسَنَّمُ الْقَبْرُ

Baked brick and wood are disliked, and there is no harm in reeds. Then soil is poured over it and the grave is made hump-shaped and not flattened.

Ruling on Infant Born Alive vs Stillborn
Infant who cries at birth gets funeral rites; stillborn does not

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on funeral rites for an infant based on signs of life and identify the dalil from the Sunnah.

Core Idea
An infant who cries at birth receives full funeral rites; a stillborn is only wrapped and buried.

This passage from al-Quduri establishes the legal criterion (istihlal) for treating a newborn who dies shortly after birth as a full legal person for funeral rites. It also provides two hadith proofs that crying (or any sound) indicates life, making the funeral prayer wajib.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage rules on funeral rites for an infant who dies after birth. It distinguishes between one who cries (mustahill) and one who does not (stillborn). For the mustahill, naming, washing, and prayer are wajib; for the stillborn, only wrapping in a cloth and burial without prayer.
2
Locate the dalil
Two hadith are cited: from al-Mughirah that 'the child is prayed over,' and from Jabir that 'when the child cries, he is prayed over and inherits.'
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The hadith from Jabir directly conditions prayer on crying, so crying is the evidence of life. The first hadith establishes the general principle. Hanafi usul: the general command is specified by the condition in the second hadith.
4
Identify the criterion
The effective cause (illa) is istihlal (any sign of life after complete birth). The text emphasizes crying because it is the clearest indicator, but movement or sound suffices.
5
Note the practical difference
If any sign of life is present, full funeral rites are performed. If stillborn, only wrapping and burial without prayer.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَمَنْ اسْتَهَلَّ بَعْدَ الْوِلَادَةِ سُمِّيَ وَغُسَلَ وَصُلِّيَ عَلَيْهِ وَإِنْ لَمْ يَسْتَهِنَّ أُدْرجَ فِي خِرْقَةٍ وَلَمْ يُصَلَّ عَلَيْهِ

وجه: (1) الحديث لثبوت وَمَنْ اسْتَهَلَّ بَعْدَ الْوِلَادَةِ سُمِّيَ
عَنِ الْمُغِيرَةِ بْن شُعْبَةَ أَنَّهُ ذَكَرَ أَنَّ رَسُولَ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم قَالَ: «الرَّاكِبُ خَلْفَ الْجِنَازَةِ، وَالْمَاشِي حَيْثُ شَاءَ مِنْهَا، وَالطِّفْلُ يُصَلَّى عَلَيْهِ» (سنن نسائي، الصَّلَاةُ عَلَى الْأَطْفَالِ،،نمبر 1548)
وجه:(۲) الحديث لثبوت وَمَنْ اسْتَهَلَّ بَعْدَ الْوِلَادَةِ سُمِّيَ
عَنْ جَابِرِ بْنِ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ، قَالَ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم: «إِذَا اسْتَهَلَّ الصَّبِيُّ، صُلِّيَ عَلَيْهِ وَوُرِثَ» (سنن نسائي، بَابُ مَا جَاءَ فِي الصَّلَاةِ عَلَى الطَّفْل،،نمبر 1508)
And whoever cries after birth is named, washed, and prayed over. And if he does not cry, he is wrapped in a cloth and no prayer is offered over him.

Proof (1): Hadith for 'whoever cries after birth is named': From al-Mughirah ibn Shu'bah that he mentioned that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'The rider goes behind the funeral, and the pedestrian wherever he wishes from it, and the child is prayed over.' (Sunan al-Nasa'i, Prayer over Children, no. 1548)
Proof (2): Hadith for 'whoever cries after birth is named': From Jabir ibn Abdillah, he said: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'When the child cries, he is prayed over and inherits.' (Sunan al-Nasa'i, Chapter on Prayer over the Child, no. 1508)
Source pages p. 184

Commentary
This passage states the ruling regarding an infant who dies shortly after birth. The criterion for receiving full funeral rites (naming, washing, and funeral prayer) is istihlal – that the infant cries or makes any audible sound indicating life after complete birth (i.e., after the whole body has emerged). If the infant shows no sign of life (stillborn), it is only wrapped in a cloth (khirqah) and buried, without the funeral prayer. The hadith proofs are from al-Mughirah and Jabir, both confirming that the child who cries (mustahill) is prayed over. The hadith from Jabir also mentions that such a child inherits, which indicates legal personhood.

Key Terms
اِسْتَهَلَّ (istahalla): To cry or make a sound at birth; to show signs of life
خِرْقَة (khirqah): A piece of cloth for wrapping the stillborn infant

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on the funeral prayer for an infant who cries at birth but then dies?
A) The prayer is not performed because the infant is a minor.
B) The prayer is performed because the infant showed signs of life.
C) The prayer is performed only if the infant lived for a few days.
D) The prayer is not performed; only washing is done.

Key Takeaway
The distinguishing factor for funeral rites is the presence of any sign of life after complete birth; crying is the primary indicator but not the exclusive one.

The Martyr: Definition, Ruling, and the Junub Dispute
Definition and internal dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of the complete martyr (shahid kamil) and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the washing of a junub or minor martyr, citing the hadith of Hanzalah.

Core Idea
A complete martyr is not washed, but a junub martyr is washed according to Abu Hanifa — the hadith of Hanzalah determines the exception.

This passage from the Quduri opens the chapter on the martyr (shahid). It first defines who qualifies as a complete martyr who is not washed, then presents an internal Hanafi dispute: what if the martyr was in a state of janabah or was a minor? Abu Hanifa argues they must be washed, while the Sahibayn disagree. Understanding this dispute reveals how specific textual evidence (the hadith of Hanzalah) can override a general rule in Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three categories of complete martyr
From the passage, list the three conditions that make a person a 'complete martyr' (shahid kamil) who is not washed: killed by polytheists, found dead on battlefield with wound traces, or killed unjustly by Muslims without blood-money.
These are the only types exempt from washing per the Hanafi school.
2
Extract the general ruling for a complete martyr
State the three actions: he is shrouded, prayed over, and not washed. Note that the four hadith proofs cited support this ruling by showing the Prophet's practice at Uhud.
The hadith 'Bury them in their blood' is the primary evidence.
3
Locate the intra-Hanafi dispute
Read the line: 'وَإِذَا اسْتُشْهِدَ الْجُنُبُ غُسَلَ عِنْدَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ وَكَذَا الصَّبِيُّ وَقَالَ أَبُو يُوسُفَ وَمُحَمَّدٌ لَا يُغَسَّلَانِ'. Identify the two positions: Abu Hanifa washes, Sahibayn do not.
This is an ikhtilaf within the Hanafi school.
4
Analyze the evidence for each position
Abu Hanifa uses the hadith of Hanzalah (washed by angels) as proof that janabah necessitates washing. The Sahibayn hold that the general rule of not washing martyrs covers all, and the Hanzalah hadith refers to angelic washing, not human.
The dispute turns on whether the specific text overrides the general.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf and mufta bihi
The practical difference: if a junub martyr is found, Abu Hanifa's followers wash him; Sahibayn's followers do not. Later Hanafi fatwa generally follows Abu Hanifa for the junub, with some variation for minors.
The mufta bihi for junub is to wash; for minors, there is difference.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بَابُ الشَّهِيدِ

الشَّهِيدُ مَنْ قَتَلَهُ الْمُشْرِكُونَ أَوْ وُجِدَ فِي الْمَعْرَكَةِ وَبِهِ أَثَرٌ أَوْ قَتَلَهُ الْمُسْلِمُونَ ظُلْمًا وَلَمْ يَجِبْ بِقَتْلِهِ دِيَةٌ فَيُكَفَّنُ وَيُصَلَّى عَلَيْهِ وَلَا يُغَسَّلُ . وَإِذَا اسْتُشْهِدَ الْجُنُبُ غُسَلَ عِنْدَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ وَكَذَا الصَّبِيُّ وَقَالَ أَبُو يُوسُفَ وَمُحَمَّدٌ لَا يُغَسَّلَانِ

وجه: (1) الحديث لثبوت فَيُكَفَّنُ وَيُصَلَّى عَلَيْهِ وَلَا يُغَسَّلُ
عَنْ جَابِرٍ قَالَ: قَالَ النَّبِيُّ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ: «ادْفِنُوهُمْ فِي دِمَائِهِمْ. يَعْنِي يَوْمَ أُحُدٍ، وَلَمْ يُغَسَلْهُمْ.» (بخاري شريف: باب من لم ير غسل الشهداء، نمبر 1346 سنن ابوداؤد باب في الشهيد يغسل،نمبر 3135)
وجه:(۲) الحديث لثبوت فَيُكَفَّنُ وَيُصَلَّى عَلَيْهِ
عَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ قَالَ: «أَمَرَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم بِقَتْلَى أحدٍ، أَنْ يُنزَعَ عَنْهُمُ الْحَدِيدُ وَالجُلُودُ، وَأَنْ يُدْفَنُوا بِدِمَائِهِمْ وَثِيَابِهِمْ (ابوداؤد: في الشهيد يغسل، 3134)
وجه (۳) الحديث لثبوت فَيُكَفَّنُ وَيُصَلَّى عَلَيْهِ وَلَا يُغَسَّلُ
عَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ، قَالَ: أُتِيَ بِهِمْ رَسُولَ الله صلى الله عليه وسلم يَوْمَ أُحُدٍ، فَجَعَلَ يُصَلِّي عَلَى عَشَرَةٍ عَشَرَةٍ، وَحَمْزَةُ هُوَ كَمَا هُوَ، يُرْفَعُونَ وَهُوَ كَمَا هُوَ مَوْضُوع (سنن ابن ماجه (۲۸) باب ما جاء في الصلاة على الشهداء ودفنهم،نمبر 1513)
وجه (۴) الحديث لثبوت فَيُكَفَّنُ وَيُصَلَّى عَلَيْهِ وَلَا يُغَسَّلُ
عَنْ عُقْبَةَ بْن عَامِرٍ : «أَنَّ النَّبِيَّ صلى الله عليه وسلم خَرَجَ يَوْمًا فَصَلَّى عَلَى أَهْلِ أُحُدٍ صَلَاتَهُ عَلَى الْمَيِّتِ، ثُمَّ انْصَرَفَ إِلَى الْمِنْبَرِ (بخاري شريف: باب الصلاة على الشهيد، نمبر 1344)
وجه:(1) دليل الشافعي الحديث لثبوت الشَّهِيدُ مَنْ قَتَلَهُ الْمُشْرِكُونَ
عَنْ جَابِرِ بْنِ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ رضي الله عنهما قَالَ: «...وَأَمَرَ بِدَفْنِهِمْ فِي دِمَائِهِمْ، وَلَمْ يُغَسَلُوا، وَلَمْ يُصَلَّ عَلَيْهِمْ.» (بخاري شريف: باب الصلاة على الشهيد نمبر 1343 سنن ابوداؤد باب في الشهيد يغسل، نمبر 3135)
وجه : (۱) الحديث لثبوت وَإِذَا اسْتُشْهِدَ الْجُنُبُ غُسَلَ
حَدَّثَنِي يَحْيَى بْنُ عَبَّادِ بْنِ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ حَنْظَلَةَ بْنَ أَبِي عَامِرٍ، قَالَ: فَقَالَ رَسُولُ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم : " إِنَّ صَاحِبَكُمْ تُغَسِلُهُ الْمَلَائِكَةُ (سنن بيهقي: باب الجنب يستشهد في المعركة ، نمبر 6814 مستدرك للحاكم : ذكر مناقب حنظلة . بن عبد الله. 4917)

اصول : کامل شہید (جس کو کفار نے قتل کیا ہو یا معرکہ جنگ میں زخمی پایا جائے یا اس کو ظلما قتل ہوا ہو کہ اس کی دیت واجب نہ ہوئی ہو) کو غسل نہیں دیا جائے، البتہ کفن دیا جائے گا اور نماز بھی ادا کی جائے۔
Chapter of the Martyr

The martyr is one whom the polytheists kill, or who is found on the battlefield with a trace (of wounds), or who is killed unjustly by Muslims and no blood-money is obligatory for his killing. He is shrouded and prayed over, but not washed. And if a junub (sexually defiled) person is martyred, he is washed according to Abu Hanifah, and likewise a minor. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said: Both are not washed.

Proof (1): Hadith for 'He is shrouded and prayed over but not washed': From Jabir, he said: The Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Bury them in their blood,' meaning on the Day of Uhud, and he did not wash them. (Bukhari, Chapter: Those who did not wash the martyrs, no. 1346; Abu Dawud, Chapter: Washing the martyr, no. 3135)
Proof (2): Hadith for 'He is shrouded and prayed over': From Ibn Abbas, he said: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) commanded regarding the slain of Uhud that the iron and leather be removed from them, and that they be buried in their blood and their clothes. (Abu Dawud, on washing the martyr, 3134)
Proof (3): Hadith for 'He is shrouded and prayed over but not washed': From Ibn Abbas, he said: They were brought to the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) on the day of Uhud, and he began to pray over ten at a time, while Hamzah remained as he was; they were lifted and he remained in place. (Ibn Majah, Chapter: What came about praying over martyrs and burying them, no. 1513)
Proof (4): Hadith for 'He is shrouded and prayed over but not washed': From Uqbah ibn Amir: The Prophet (peace be upon him) went out one day and prayed over the people of Uhud like his prayer over the deceased, then turned to the pulpit. (Bukhari, Chapter: Prayer over the martyr, no. 1344)
Proof (1): Shafi'i's evidence for the definition 'The martyr is one whom the polytheists kill': From Jabir ibn Abdillah, he said: '...and he commanded to bury them in their blood; they were not washed nor prayed over.' (Bukhari, Chapter: Prayer over the martyr, no. 1343; Abu Dawud, Chapter: Washing the martyr, no. 3135)
Proof (1): Hadith for 'If a junub is martyred, he is washed': Yahya ibn Abbad ibn Abdullah narrated that Hanzalah ibn Abi Amir said: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'Your companion is washed by the angels.' (Baihaqi, Chapter: The junub martyred in battle, no. 6814; Mustadrak al-Hakim, mentioning the virtues of Hanzalah, 4917)

Principle: The complete martyr (one killed by disbelievers, or found wounded on the battlefield, or killed unjustly such that no blood-money is due) is not given a bath; however he is shrouded and the funeral prayer is offered.
Source pages p. 185

Commentary
This passage opens the chapter on the martyr (shahid). The text first defines who qualifies as a shahid under the category of 'complete martyr' (shahid kamil) who is not washed: (1) one killed directly by polytheists in battle, (2) one found dead on the battlefield with visible signs of wounds, and (3) one killed unjustly by Muslims without blood-money being obligatory (e.g., a tax-collector killed by rebels). Such a martyr is to be shrouded and prayed over, but not washed, with the blood left on him as a sign of honor. Four hadith proofs are given: the Prophet's command to bury the martyrs of Uhud in their blood without washing, the removal of iron and leather but retention of blood and clothes, the Prophet praying over them in groups, and the prayer over the martyrs after the battle. Next, an intra-Hanafi dispute is presented: Abu Hanifah rules that if a person in a state of janabah is martyred, he must be washed before burial, and likewise a minor (who has not reached puberty) is washed. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (al-Shaybani) hold that neither is washed, because the general rule of not washing martyrs applies to all, and the hadith about Hanzalah (who was junub at death) indicates that he was washed by angels, not humans. The text then presents the hadith of Hanzalah as proof for Abu Hanifah's position. Finally, the Urdu summary confirms that the complete martyr is not washed, but is shrouded and prayed over.

Key Terms
شَهِيد (shahīd): A person killed in a specific manner as defined by the Hanafi school: killed by disbelievers, found dead on battlefield with wounds, or killed unjustly by Muslims without blood-money.
جُنُب (junub): A person in a state of major ritual impurity requiring ghusl

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi (relied-upon position) in the Hanafi school, what should be done with a martyr who died in a state of janabah?
A) He is not washed, like any other martyr.
B) He must be washed to remove the janabah, then shrouded and prayed over.
C) He is washed only if there is no water available.
D) He is not washed and the funeral prayer is also not offered.

Key Takeaway
A complete martyr is not washed, but if the martyr is in a state of janabah or is a minor, Abu Hanifa requires washing — a key exception to the general rule.

Definition and Basic Ruling of the Martyr (Shahid)
Defines shahid and gives the ruling of no washing but shrouding and prayer, with intra-Hanafi dispute on junub and child

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define the Hanafi shahid, state the ruling that the complete martyr is not washed but is shrouded and prayed upon, and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the junub and child martyr.

Core Idea
The Hanafi shahid is not washed but is shrouded and prayed upon; the junub and child martyr are subject to dispute.

This passage from Al-Quduri's Mukhtasar defines who qualifies as a shahid (martyr) in Hanafi law and gives the corresponding funeral ruling. It then presents an internal Hanafi disagreement about whether the rule of no washing applies when the martyr was in a state of major impurity (junub) or was a child. Understanding this definition is crucial for correctly applying the janazah rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three conditions of a shahid
Extract from the text the three scenarios that make a person a complete martyr: killed by polytheists, found dead on battlefield with a wound, or killed unjustly by Muslims with no blood money.
The third condition includes the absence of a mandatory diyah.
2
State the basic ruling for the complete martyr
The complete martyr is not washed; rather, he is shrouded and the funeral prayer (salat al-janazah) is offered over him.
This is the default ruling for a shahid.
3
Recognize the intra-Hanafi dispute
Note that Imam Abu Hanifa holds that a martyr in janabah (major impurity) and a child martyr are washed, while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani hold that they are not washed, like other martyrs.
The dispute is recorded but no explicit tarjih is given in this passage.
4
Understand the evidence for the dispute
Abu Hanifa relies on the hadith of Hanzalah (whose body was washed by angels) to argue that the junub martyr is washed. The Sahibayn rely on the general proofs that martyrs are not washed.
The hadith of Hanzalah is specific to the janabah case.
5
Apply the ruling to a practical scenario
Given a martyr who meets the three conditions, decide whether washing is required if he was junub or a child, noting which imam's view you follow.
The thamarah al-khilaf: the actual practice differs based on the preferred opinion.
