بَابُ الشَّهِيدِ
بَابُ الشَّهِيدِ
ل الشَّهِيدُ مَنْ قَتَلَهُ الْمُشْرِكُونَ أَوْ وُجِدَ فِي الْمَعْرَكَةِ وَبِهِ أَثَرٌ أَوْ قَتَلَهُ الْمُسْلِمُونَ ظُلْمًا وَلَمْ يَجِبْ بِقَتْلِهِ دِيَةٌ لِّ فَيُكَفَّنُ وَيُصَلَّى عَلَيْهِ وَلَا يُعَسَّلُ . وَإِذَا أَسْتُشْهِدَ الْجُنُبُ غُسَلَ عِنْدَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ وَكَذَا الصَّبِيُّ وَقَالَ أَبُو يُوسُفَ وَمُحَمَّدٌ لَا يُغَسَّلَانِ ل وجه: (1) الحديث لثبوت فَيُكَفَّنُ وَيُصَلَّى عَلَيْهِ وَلَا يُعَسَّلُ \ عَنْ جَابِرٍ قَالَ: قَالَ النَّبِيُّ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ: «ادْفِنُوهُمْ فِي دِمَائِهِمْ. يَعْنِي يَوْمَ أُحُدٍ، وَلَمْ يُغَسَلْهُمْ.» (بخاري شريف: باب من لم يغسل الشهداء، نمبر 1346 سنن ابوداؤد باب في الشهيد يغسل،نمبر 3135) وجه:(۲) الحديث لثبوت فَيُكَفَّنُ وَيُصَلَّى عَلَيْهِ عَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ قَالَ: «أَمَرَرَسُولُ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم بِقَتْلَى أحدٍ، أَنْ يُنزَعَ عَنْهُمُ الْحَدِيدُ وَالجُلُودُ، وَأَنْ يُدْفَنُوا بِدِمَائِهِمْ وَثِيَاتِهِمْ (ابوداؤد: في الشهيد يغسل، 3134) وجه (۳) الحديث لثبوت فَيُكَفَّنُ وَيُصَلَّى عَلَيْهِ وَلَا يُعَسَّلُ \ عَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ، قَالَ: أُتِيَ بِهِمْ رَسُولَ الله صلى الله عليه وسلم يَوْمَ أُحُدٍ، فَجَعَلَ يُصَلِّي عَلَى عَشَرَةٍ عَشَرَةٍ، وَحَمْزَةُ هُوَ كَمَا هُوَ، يُرْفَعُونَ وَهُوَ كَمَا هُوَ مَوْضُوع (سنن ابن ماجه (۲۸) باب ما جاء في الصلاة على الشهداء ودفنهم،نمبر 1513) وجه (۴) الحديث لثبوت فَيُكَفَّنُ وَيُصَلَّى عَلَيْهِ وَلَا يُغَسَّلُ \ عَنْ عُقْبَةَ بْن عَامِرٍ : «أَنَّ النَّبِيَّ صلى الله عليه وسلم خَرَجَ يَوْمًا فَصَلَّى عَلَى أَهْلِ أُحُدٍ صَلَاتَهُ عَلَى الْمَيِّتِ، ثُمَّ انْصَرَفَ إِلَى الْمِنْبَرِ (بخاري شريف: باب الصلاة على الشهيد، نمبر 1344)
وجه:(1) دليل الشافعي الحديث لثبوت الشَّهِيدُ مَنْ قَتَلَهُ الْمُشْرِكُونَ \ عَنْ جَابِرِ بْنِ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ رضي الله عنهما قَالَ: ٠.٠٠٠ وَأَمَرَ بِدَفْنِهِمْ فِي دِمَائِهِمْ، وَلَمْ يُغَسَلُوا، وَلَمْ يُصَلَّ عَلَيْهِمْ.» (بخاري شريف: باب الصلاة على الشهيد نمبر 1343 سنن ابوداؤد باب في الشهيد يغسل، نمبر 3135) وجه : (۱) الحديث لثبوت وَإِذَا اسْتُشْهِدَ الْجُنُبُ غُسَلَ \ حَدَّثَنِي يَحْيَى بْنُ عَبَّادِ بْنِ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ حَنْظَلَةَ بْنَ أَبِي عَامِرٍ، قَالَ: فَقَالَ رَسُولُ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم : " إِنَّ صَاحِبَكُمْ تُغَسِلُهُ الْمَلَائِكَةُ (سنن بيهقي: باب الجنب يستشهد في المعركة ، نمبر 6814 مستدرك للحاكم : ذكر مناقب حنظلة . بن عبد الله. 4917) اصول : کامل شہید (جس کو کفار نے قتل کیا ہو یا معرکہ جنگ میں زخمی پایا جائے یا اس کو ظلما قتل ہوا ہو کہ اس کی دیت واجب نہ ہوئی ہو) کو غسل نہیں دیا جائے، البتہ کفن دیا جائے گا اور نماز بھی ادا کی جائے۔
Chapter of the Martyr. The martyr is: one whom the polytheists kill, or one found on the battlefield with a wound, or one killed unjustly by Muslims such that no blood money is obligatory for his killing. So he is shrouded and prayer is offered over him, and he is not washed. And when a person in major impurity (junub) is martyred, he is washed according to Abu Hanifa, and likewise a child. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said: they are not washed. [Hadith proofs follow] Principle: The complete martyr (one killed by disbelievers, or found wounded on battlefield, or killed unjustly such that his blood money is not obligatory) is not given a bath; however, he will be shrouded and the funeral prayer will be performed over him.
Source pages p. 185

Commentary
This passage from Al-Quduri defines the shahid (martyr) in Hanafi fiqh and states the basic ruling: the complete martyr is not washed but is shrouded and the funeral prayer (salat al-janazah) is offered. Three conditions identify a complete martyr: (1) killed by polytheists in battle; (2) found dead on the battlefield with a wound; (3) killed unjustly by Muslims in a way that no diyah (blood money) is required. The text then presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding a martyr who is in a state of janabah (major impurity) or a child. Imam Abu Hanifa holds that they are washed, while the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say they are not washed. Multiple hadith proofs are cited for the basic ruling (e.g., the Prophet's treatment of the martyrs of Uhud) and for the dispute (the story of Hanzalah, whom the angels washed). The Urdu conclusion repeats the definition and ruling.

Key Terms
شَهِيد (shahīd): One who meets one of three conditions: killed by polytheists, found dead on battlefield with wound, or killed unjustly by Muslims without blood money.
جُنُب (junub): A person in a state of major ritual impurity requiring ghusl.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, what is the ruling on washing a martyr who was in a state of janabah (major impurity)?
A) The martyr is not washed at all.
B) The martyr is washed because of the hadith of Hanzalah.
C) The martyr is washed only if he was an adult.
D) The ruling depends on the type of wound.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi shahid is defined by three conditions and is not washed, but is shrouded and prayed upon, with an internal dispute on the junub and child martyr.

Martyr Burial: Blood and Clothes
Details the burial practice for the martyr.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on washing the martyr's blood and removing his clothes, and identify which items are removed.

Core Idea
The martyr is buried with his blood and clothes; only certain items are removed.

The previous lesson established that the martyr is not washed. Now the text details what is done with his blood and clothes. This seemingly minor point has deep significance: it preserves the honor of his sacrifice and follows the sunnah of the Prophet ﷺ at Uhud.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act
What physical actions are prescribed for the martyr's body? Note the two prohibitions: not washing the blood, and not removing clothes.
2
List the exceptions
The text then lists items that ARE removed: fur coat, khuff, turban, and weapons. Understand why: these are not part of the usual burial shroud or are possessions.
The hadith from Ibn Abbas supports: 'Remove iron and leather, bury them with their blood and clothes.'
3
Connect to the dalil
The hadith from Ibn Abbas is the proof. Explain how it directly commands the removal of iron and leather, which the Hanafis interpret as the items listed.
Other schools may have different lists.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

وَلَا يُغْسَلَ عَنْ الشَّهِيدِ دَمُهُ وَلَا تُنْزَعُ عَنْهُ ثِيَابُهُ وَيُنْزَعُ عَنْهُ الْفَرْوُ وَالْخَفُّ وَالْخَشْوَ وَالسَّلَاحُ ه وَمَنْ اُرْتُثَ غُسَلَ وَالِارْتِثَاتُ أَنْ يَأْكُلَ أَوْ يَشْرَبَ أَوْ يَتَدَاوَى أَوْ يَبْقَى حَيَّا حَتَّى يَقْضِيَ عَلَيْهِ وَقْتُ صَلَاةٍ وَهُوَ يَعْقِلُ أَوْ يُنْقَلُ مِنْ الْمَعْرَكَةِ وَهُوَ يَعْقِلُ ل وَمَنْ قُتِلَ فِي حَدٍ أَوْ قِصَاصِ غُسَلَ وَصُلِّيَ عَلَيْهِ وَمَنْ قُتِلَ مِنْ الْبُغَاةِ أَوْ قُطَّاعِ الطَّرِيقِ لَمَّ يُصَلَّ عَلَيْهِ وَلَمْ يُغَسَّلْ
وجه : (1) الحديث لثبوت وَلَا يُغْسَلُ عَنْ الشَّهِيدِ دَمُهُ وَلَا تُنْزَعُ عَنْهُ ثِيَابُهُ \ عَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ قَالَ: «أَمَرَ رَسُولُ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم بِقَتْلَى أَحَدٍ، أَنْ يُنْزَعَ عَنْهُمُ الْحَدِيدُ وَالْجُلُودُ، وَأَنْ يُدْفَنُوا بِدِمَائِهِمْ وَثِيَابِهِمْ . » ( سنن ابوداؤد باب في الشهيد يغسل نمبر 3134 سنن ابن ماجه: (۲۸) باب ما جاء في الصلاة على الشهداء ودفنهم،نمبر 1515)
د. وجه : (۱) قول الصحابي لثبوت وَمَنْ أَرْتُنَّ غُسِلَ وَالِارْتِثَاتُ أَنْ يَأْكُلَ \ عَنْ عَمْرِو بْنِ مَيْمُونٍ فِي قِصَّةِ قَتْلِ عُمَرَ حِينَ طَعَنَهُ، قَالَ : فَطَارَ الْعِلْجُ بِالسِّكِّينِ ذَاتِ طَرَفَيْنِ لَا يَمُرُّ عَلَى أَحَدٍ يَمِينًا وَلَا شِمَالًا إِلَّا طَعَنَهُ. وَفِي ذَلِكَ دَلَالَةٌ عَلَى أَنَّهُ قُتِلَ بِمِحْدَدٍ ثُمَّ غُسَلَ وَكُفَّنَ وَصْلِيَ عَلَيْهِ (سنن بيهقي: باب المرتث والذي يقتل ظلما في غير معترك الكفار والذي يرجع إليه سيفه، نمبر 6820) د وجه : (1) الحديث لثبوت وَمَنْ قُتِلَ فِي حَةٍ أَوْ قِصَاصِ غُسَلَ وَصُلِّيَ عَلَيْهِ \ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ بْنِ بُرَيْدَةَ، عَنْ أَبِيهِ فِي قِصَّةِ الْغَامِدِيَّةِ الَّتِي رُجِمَتْ فِي الزِّنَا، قَالَ النَّبِيُّ صلى الله عليه وسلم : " فَوَالَّذِي نَفْسِي بِيَدِهِ لَقَدْ تَابَتْ تَوْبَةً لَوْ تَابَهَا صَاحِبُ مَكْسٍ لَغْفِرَ لَهُ، ثُمَّ أَمَرَ بِمَا فَصَلَّى عَلَيْهَا وَدُفِنَتْ (سنن بيهقي: بَابُ الصَّلَاةِ عَلَى مَنْ قَتَلَتْهُ الخُدُودُ، نمبر 6830)
ك وجه:(۱) الحديث لثبوت وَمَنْ قُتِلَ مِنْ الْبُغَاةِ أَوْ قُطَّاعِ الطَّرِيقِ \ عَنْ جَابِرِ بْنِ سَمُرَةَ، قَالَ: " أُتِيَ النَّبِيُّ صلى الله عليه وسلم بِرَجُلٍ قَتَلَ نَظْسَهُ بِمَشَاقِصَ فَلَمْ يُصَلِ عَلَيْهِ (سنن بيهقي: بَابُ الصَّلَاةِ عَلَى مَنْ قَتَلَ نَفْسَةَ غَيْرَ مُسْتَحِلَّ لِقَتْلِهَا ، نمبر 6833)
اصول: اگر کسی شخص کو حربی یا باغی یا پھر چور مار ڈالیں تو وہ شخص بھی شہید کے حکم میں ہے۔ اصول شہر میں جو مقتول ملے تو وہ شہید نہیں ہے الا یہ کہ شہادت کی کوئی علامت ظاہر ہو جائے۔
Chapter of the Martyr. His blood is not washed from him, nor are his clothes removed; the fur coat, khuff (leather socks), turban, and weapons are removed. And one who is murtath (lingers after battle) is washed. Al-irtithath is that he eats, drinks, treats himself, remains alive until the time of a prayer passes while conscious, or is moved from the battlefield while conscious. And one killed in a prescribed punishment (hadd) or retaliation (qisas) is washed and prayed over. And one killed among the rebels (baghi) or highway robbers (qutta' al-tariq) is not prayed over nor washed. [Hadith proofs follow] Principle: If a person is killed by a harbi (enemy combatant), a baghi (rebel), or a thief, then that person is also in the ruling of a martyr. Principle: One who is found killed in the city is not a martyr unless some sign of martyrdom appears.
Source pages p. 186

Commentary
This passage continues the chapter on the martyr, providing specific practical rulings. First, the martyr's blood is not washed off, and his clothes are not removed, except for items like fur coats, khuff (leather socks), turbans, and weapons. Second, if the wounded person is 'murtath' — meaning he eats, drinks, receives treatment, remains conscious through a full prayer time, or is moved from the battlefield while conscious — he loses the special status and is washed and prayed over as a normal deceased. Third, those executed for hadd offenses (e.g., stoning for adultery) or qisas (retaliation) are washed and the funeral prayer is offered; they are not considered martyrs. Fourth, rebels (baghi) and highway robbers (qutta' al-tariq) who are killed are not washed nor is prayer offered over them, as they are considered sinful aggressors. The hadith proofs support each ruling: the martyr of Uhud were buried with blood and clothes (except iron and leather); the story of Umar's assassination shows that the murder victim is washed; the Ghamidiyyah who was stoned was prayed over; and a suicide was not prayed over. The Urdu summary adds that one killed by a harbi, baghi, or thief is considered a martyr, but one found killed in the city is not unless signs of martyrdom are present.

Key Terms
فَرْو (farw): Fur coat, a garment of animal fur.
خُفّ (khuff): Leather socks worn inside shoes.
خَشْو (khashw): Turban or head wrap.
سِلاح (silah): Weapons.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT removed from the martyr's body?
A) Fur coat
B) Khuff (leather socks)
C) Shirt (qamis)
D) Turban

Key Takeaway
The martyr is buried with his blood and clothes except for fur, khuff, turban, and weapons, following the sunnah of Uhud.

The Murtath: Definition and Ruling
Defines irtithath and its ruling.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define irtithath and state the ruling for a murtath: that he is washed and prayed over.

Core Idea
A wounded fighter who shows signs of life after battle loses martyr status and is treated as a normal deceased.

The term 'murtath' refers to a wounded person who survives the battle and engages in worldly acts like eating, drinking, or receiving treatment. The Hanafi school defines clear criteria that remove the special martyr ruling. Understanding these criteria is essential to avoid misapplying the martyr's privileges.

Guided Path
1
Define irtithath
From the text, list the actions that constitute irtithath: eating, drinking, treating, remaining conscious through a prayer time, or being moved conscious.
These actions indicate the person was not killed instantly and thus not a full martyr.
2
Derive the ruling
Since the murtath shows signs of normal life, the text says he is washed and prayed over. Understand that this means the martyr's burial privileges are removed.
3
Examine the proof
The proof cited is the story of Umar's assassination: he was washed and prayed over despite being killed by a disbeliever. This shows that if the victim survives long enough, he is not a martyr in the full sense.
The hadith is from the action of the Companions after Umar's death.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بَابُ الشَّهِيدِ
وَلَا يُغْسَلَ عَنْ الشَّهِيدِ دَمُهُ وَلَا تُنْزَعُ عَنْهُ ثِيَابُهُ وَيُنْزَعُ عَنْهُ الْفَرْوُ وَالْخَفُّ وَالْخَشْوَ وَالسَّلَاحُ ه وَمَنْ اُرْتُثَ غُسَلَ وَالِارْتِثَاتُ أَنْ يَأْكُلَ أَوْ يَشْرَبَ أَوْ يَتَدَاوَى أَوْ يَبْقَى حَيَّا حَتَّى يَقْضِيَ عَلَيْهِ وَقْتُ صَلَاةٍ وَهُوَ يَعْقِلُ أَوْ يُنْقَلُ مِنْ الْمَعْرَكَةِ وَهُوَ يَعْقِلُ ل وَمَنْ قُتِلَ فِي حَدٍ أَوْ قِصَاصِ غُسَلَ وَصُلِّيَ عَلَيْهِ وَمَنْ قُتِلَ مِنْ الْبُغَاةِ أَوْ قُطَّاعِ الطَّرِيقِ لَمَّ يُصَلَّ عَلَيْهِ وَلَمْ يُغَسَّلْ
وجه : (1) الحديث لثبوت وَلَا يُغْسَلُ عَنْ الشَّهِيدِ دَمُهُ وَلَا تُنْزَعُ عَنْهُ ثِيَابُهُ \ عَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ قَالَ: «أَمَرَ رَسُولُ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم بِقَتْلَى أَحَدٍ، أَنْ يُنْزَعَ عَنْهُمُ الْحَدِيدُ وَالْجُلُودُ، وَأَنْ يُدْفَنُوا بِدِمَائِهِمْ وَثِيَابِهِمْ . » ( سنن ابوداؤد باب في الشهيد يغسل نمبر 3134 سنن ابن ماجه: (۲۸) باب ما جاء في الصلاة على الشهداء ودفنهم،نمبر 1515)
د. وجه : (۱) قول الصحابي لثبوت وَمَنْ أَرْتُنَّ غُسِلَ وَالِارْتِثَاتُ أَنْ يَأْكُلَ \ عَنْ عَمْرِو بْنِ مَيْمُونٍ فِي قِصَّةِ قَتْلِ عُمَرَ حِينَ طَعَنَهُ، قَالَ : فَطَارَ الْعِلْجُ بِالسِّكِّينِ ذَاتِ طَرَفَيْنِ لَا يَمُرُّ عَلَى أَحَدٍ يَمِينًا وَلَا شِمَالًا إِلَّا طَعَنَهُ. وَفِي ذَلِكَ دَلَالَةٌ عَلَى أَنَّهُ قُتِلَ بِمِحْدَدٍ ثُمَّ غُسَلَ وَكُفَّنَ وَصْلِيَ عَلَيْهِ (سنن بيهقي: باب المرتث والذي يقتل ظلما في غير معترك الكفار والذي يرجع إليه سيفه، نمبر 6820) د وجه : (1) الحديث لثبوت وَمَنْ قُتِلَ فِي حَةٍ أَوْ قِصَاصِ غُسَلَ وَصُلِّيَ عَلَيْهِ \ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ بْنِ بُرَيْدَةَ، عَنْ أَبِيهِ فِي قِصَّةِ الْغَامِدِيَّةِ الَّتِي رُجِمَتْ فِي الزِّنَا، قَالَ النَّبِيُّ صلى الله عليه وسلم : " فَوَالَّذِي نَفْسِي بِيَدِهِ لَقَدْ تَابَتْ تَوْبَةً لَوْ تَابَهَا صَاحِبُ مَكْسٍ لَغْفِرَ لَهُ، ثُمَّ أَمَرَ بِمَا فَصَلَّى عَلَيْهَا وَدُفِنَتْ (سنن بيهقي: بَابُ الصَّلَاةِ عَلَى مَنْ قَتَلَتْهُ الخُدُودُ، نمبر 6830)
ك وجه:(۱) الحديث لثبوت وَمَنْ قُتِلَ مِنْ الْبُغَاةِ أَوْ قُطَّاعِ الطَّرِيقِ \ عَنْ جَابِرِ بْنِ سَمُرَةَ، قَالَ: " أُتِيَ النَّبِيُّ صلى الله عليه وسلم بِرَجُلٍ قَتَلَ نَظْسَهُ بِمَشَاقِصَ فَلَمْ يُصَلِ عَلَيْهِ (سنن بيهقي: بَابُ الصَّلَاةِ عَلَى مَنْ قَتَلَ نَفْسَةَ غَيْرَ مُسْتَحِلَّ لِقَتْلِهَا ، نمبر 6833)
اصول: اگر کسی شخص کو حربی یا باغی یا پھر چور مار ڈالیں تو وہ شخص بھی شہید کے حکم میں ہے۔ اصول شہر میں جو مقتول ملے تو وہ شہید نہیں ہے الا یہ کہ شہادت کی کوئی علامت ظاہر ہو جائے۔
Chapter of the Martyr. His blood is not washed from him, nor are his clothes removed; the fur coat, khuff (leather socks), turban, and weapons are removed. And one who is murtath (lingers after battle) is washed. Al-irtithath is that he eats, drinks, treats himself, remains alive until the time of a prayer passes while conscious, or is moved from the battlefield while conscious. And one killed in a prescribed punishment (hadd) or retaliation (qisas) is washed and prayed over. And one killed among the rebels (baghi) or highway robbers (qutta' al-tariq) is not prayed over nor washed. [Hadith proofs follow] Principle: If a person is killed by a harbi (enemy combatant), a baghi (rebel), or a thief, then that person is also in the ruling of a martyr. Principle: One who is found killed in the city is not a martyr unless some sign of martyrdom appears.
Source pages p. 186

Commentary
This passage continues the chapter on the martyr, providing specific practical rulings. First, the martyr's blood is not washed off, and his clothes are not removed, except for items like fur coats, khuff (leather socks), turbans, and weapons. Second, if the wounded person is 'murtath' — meaning he eats, drinks, receives treatment, remains conscious through a full prayer time, or is moved from the battlefield while conscious — he loses the special status and is washed and prayed over as a normal deceased. Third, those executed for hadd offenses (e.g., stoning for adultery) or qisas (retaliation) are washed and the funeral prayer is offered; they are not considered martyrs. Fourth, rebels (baghi) and highway robbers (qutta' al-tariq) who are killed are not washed nor is prayer offered over them, as they are considered sinful aggressors. The hadith proofs support each ruling: the martyr of Uhud were buried with blood and clothes (except iron and leather); the story of Umar's assassination shows that the murder victim is washed; the Ghamidiyyah who was stoned was prayed over; and a suicide was not prayed over. The Urdu summary adds that one killed by a harbi, baghi, or thief is considered a martyr, but one found killed in the city is not unless signs of martyrdom are present.

Key Terms
ارْتِثَاث (irtithath): The state of a wounded person who survives the battle and engages in one of five actions: eat, drink, treat, remain conscious through a prayer time, or be moved conscious.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT a criterion for irtithath?
A) Eating food
B) Being moved while unconscious
C) Receiving medical treatment
D) Remaining conscious until the time of a prayer passes

Key Takeaway
A murtath is defined by five conscious actions and is washed and prayed over like any Muslim.

Those Killed in Hadd or Qisas
States the ruling for those executed for hadd or qisas.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state that a person executed for hadd or qisas is washed and prayed over, and explain the proof from the Ghamidiyyah incident.

Core Idea
Even criminals executed by the state receive the normal Muslim burial rites: washing and prayer.

The text makes a clear distinction: those killed as punishment (hadd or qisas) are not considered martyrs; they are washed and prayed over. This is based on the Prophet's treatment of the Ghamidiyyah woman who was stoned for adultery. This ruling emphasizes that capital punishment does not strip a Muslim of basic funeral rights.

Guided Path
1
Identify the category
The text says: 'Man qutila fi haddin aw qisas' - those killed in a prescribed punishment or lawful retaliation. Understand that these are legal executions.
2
State the ruling
They are washed and prayed over. This means they are treated like any other deceased Muslim, not as martyrs.
3
Analyze the proof
The proof is the hadith of the Ghamidiyyah woman who was stoned. After her execution, the Prophet ﷺ offered the funeral prayer over her. This shows that even those executed for major sins receive the prayer.
The hadith emphasizes the sincerity of her repentance, but the act of praying over her establishes the ruling.

Source Text

د. وجه : (۱) قول الصحابي لثبوت وَمَنْ أَرْتُنَّ غُسِلَ وَالِارْتِثَاتُ أَنْ يَأْكُلَ \ عَنْ عَمْرِو بْنِ مَيْمُونٍ فِي قِصَّةِ قَتْلِ عُمَرَ حِينَ طَعَنَهُ، قَالَ : فَطَارَ الْعِلْجُ بِالسِّكِّينِ ذَاتِ طَرَفَيْنِ لَا يَمُرُّ عَلَى أَحَدٍ يَمِينًا وَلَا شِمَالًا إِلَّا طَعَنَهُ. وَفِي ذَلِكَ دَلَالَةٌ عَلَى أَنَّهُ قُتِلَ بِمِحْدَدٍ ثُمَّ غُسَلَ وَكُفَّنَ وَصْلِيَ عَلَيْهِ (سنن بيهقي: باب المرتث والذي يقتل ظلما في غير معترك الكفار والذي يرجع إليه سيفه، نمبر 6820) د وجه : (1) الحديث لثبوت وَمَنْ قُتِلَ فِي حَةٍ أَوْ قِصَاصِ غُسَلَ وَصُلِّيَ عَلَيْهِ \ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ بْنِ بُرَيْدَةَ، عَنْ أَبِيهِ فِي قِصَّةِ الْغَامِدِيَّةِ الَّتِي رُجِمَتْ فِي الزِّنَا، قَالَ النَّبِيُّ صلى الله عليه وسلم : " فَوَالَّذِي نَفْسِي بِيَدِهِ لَقَدْ تَابَتْ تَوْبَةً لَوْ تَابَهَا صَاحِبُ مَكْسٍ لَغْفِرَ لَهُ، ثُمَّ أَمَرَ بِمَا فَصَلَّى عَلَيْهَا وَدُفِنَتْ (سنن بيهقي: بَابُ الصَّلَاةِ عَلَى مَنْ قَتَلَتْهُ الخُدُودُ، نمبر 6830)

And one who is murtath (lingers after battle) is washed. Al-irtithath is that he eats, drinks, treats himself, remains alive until the time of a prayer passes while conscious, or is moved from the battlefield while conscious. And one killed in a prescribed punishment (hadd) or retaliation (qisas) is washed and prayed over. And one killed among the rebels (baghi) or highway robbers (qutta' al-tariq) is not prayed over nor washed. [Hadith proofs follow] Principle: If a person is killed by a harbi (enemy combatant), a baghi (rebel), or a thief, then that person is also in the ruling of a martyr. Principle: One who is found killed in the city is not a martyr unless some sign of martyrdom appears.
Source pages p. 186

Commentary
This passage continues the chapter on the martyr, providing specific practical rulings. First, the martyr's blood is not washed off, and his clothes are not removed, except for items like fur coats, khuff (leather socks), turbans, and weapons. Second, if the wounded person is 'murtath' — meaning he eats, drinks, receives treatment, remains conscious through a full prayer time, or is moved from the battlefield while conscious — he loses the special status and is washed and prayed over as a normal deceased. Third, those executed for hadd offenses (e.g., stoning for adultery) or qisas (retaliation) are washed and the funeral prayer is offered; they are not considered martyrs. Fourth, rebels (baghi) and highway robbers (qutta' al-tariq) who are killed are not washed nor is prayer offered over them, as they are considered sinful aggressors. Key Terms
حَد (hadd): A fixed punishment prescribed by Allah, e.g., for adultery, theft, drinking.
قِصَاص (qisas): Retaliation in kind for murder or injury, prescribed by law.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi ruling for a person executed for qisas?
A) He is not washed and no prayer is offered.

Key Takeaway
Even those executed for hadd or qisas receive full Islamic burial rites: washing and janazah prayer.

Rebels and Highway Robbers: No Washing or Prayer
States the ruling for rebels and highway robbers killed in action.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state that rebels (bughat) and highway robbers (qutta' al-tariq) killed in the act are not washed nor prayed over, and identify the proof from the hadith of the suicide.

Core Idea
Those who rebel with an interpretation or commit highway robbery are denied funeral rites as a deterrent and because their death was not in a just cause.

The text draws a sharp contrast: rebels (bughat) and highway robbers (qutta' al-tariq) who are killed in fighting are not washed nor is the funeral prayer offered over them. This is based on the hadith of a man who committed suicide—the Prophet did not pray for him. The ruling serves as a deterrent and marks the distinction between those who die in conflict with legitimate authority and those who die for a just cause.

Guided Path
1
Identify the categories
Two groups: al-bughaat (rebels) and qutta' al-tariq (highway robbers). Understand that these are those who are killed while actively fighting against legitimate authority or committing violent crime.
Rebels have a valid interpretation (ta'wil); highway robbers do not.
2
State the ruling
They are not washed and no prayer is offered over them. This means they are buried in their bloodied state without rites.
This is a severe measure to show disapproval and deterrence.
3
Analyze the proof
The proof is the hadith of a man who killed himself with a spear (mashaqis). The Prophet ﷺ did not pray over him. Suicide is a major sin, and by analogy, those who die in rebellion or robbery are also sinful and thus denied the prayer.
The analogy is based on the sinfulness of their action; however, rebels with ta'wil are not considered unbelievers.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بَابُ الشَّهِيدِ
وَلَا يُغْسَلَ عَنْ الشَّهِيدِ دَمُهُ وَلَا تُنْزَعُ عَنْهُ ثِيَابُهُ وَيُنْزَعُ عَنْهُ الْفَرْوُ وَالْخَفُّ وَالْخَشْوَ وَالسَّلَاحُ ه وَمَنْ اُرْتُثَ غُسَلَ وَالِارْتِثَاتُ أَنْ يَأْكُلَ أَوْ يَشْرَبَ أَوْ يَتَدَاوَى أَوْ يَبْقَى حَيَّا حَتَّى يَقْضِيَ عَلَيْهِ وَقْتُ صَلَاةٍ وَهُوَ يَعْقِلُ أَوْ يُنْقَلُ مِنْ الْمَعْرَكَةِ وَهُوَ يَعْقِلُ ل وَمَنْ قُتِلَ فِي حَدٍ أَوْ قِصَاصِ غُسَلَ وَصُلِّيَ عَلَيْهِ وَمَنْ قُتِلَ مِنْ الْبُغَاةِ أَوْ قُطَّاعِ الطَّرِيقِ لَمَّ يُصَلَّ عَلَيْهِ وَلَمْ يُغَسَّلْ
وجه : (1) الحديث لثبوت وَلَا يُغْسَلُ عَنْ الشَّهِيدِ دَمُهُ وَلَا تُنْزَعُ عَنْهُ ثِيَابُهُ \ عَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ قَالَ: «أَمَرَ رَسُولُ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم بِقَتْلَى أَحَدٍ، أَنْ يُنْزَعَ عَنْهُمُ الْحَدِيدُ وَالْجُلُودُ، وَأَنْ يُدْفَنُوا بِدِمَائِهِمْ وَثِيَابِهِمْ . » ( سنن ابوداؤد باب في الشهيد يغسل نمبر 3134 سنن ابن ماجه: (۲۸) باب ما جاء في الصلاة على الشهداء ودفنهم،نمبر 1515)
د. وجه : (۱) قول الصحابي لثبوت وَمَنْ أَرْتُنَّ غُسِلَ وَالِارْتِثَاتُ أَنْ يَأْكُلَ \ عَنْ عَمْرِو بْنِ مَيْمُونٍ فِي قِصَّةِ قَتْلِ عُمَرَ حِينَ طَعَنَهُ، قَالَ : فَطَارَ الْعِلْجُ بِالسِّكِّينِ ذَاتِ طَرَفَيْنِ لَا يَمُرُّ عَلَى أَحَدٍ يَمِينًا وَلَا شِمَالًا إِلَّا طَعَنَهُ. وَفِي ذَلِكَ دَلَالَةٌ عَلَى أَنَّهُ قُتِلَ بِمِحْدَدٍ ثُمَّ غُسَلَ وَكُفَّنَ وَصْلِيَ عَلَيْهِ (سنن بيهقي: باب المرتث والذي يقتل ظلما في غير معترك الكفار والذي يرجع إليه سيفه، نمبر 6820) د وجه : (1) الحديث لثبوت وَمَنْ قُتِلَ فِي حَةٍ أَوْ قِصَاصِ غُسَلَ وَصُلِّيَ عَلَيْهِ \ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ بْنِ بُرَيْدَةَ، عَنْ أَبِيهِ فِي قِصَّةِ الْغَامِدِيَّةِ الَّتِي رُجِمَتْ فِي الزِّنَا، قَالَ النَّبِيُّ صلى الله عليه وسلم : " فَوَالَّذِي نَفْسِي بِيَدِهِ لَقَدْ تَابَتْ تَوْبَةً لَوْ تَابَهَا صَاحِبُ مَكْسٍ لَغْفِرَ لَهُ، ثُمَّ أَمَرَ بِمَا فَصَلَّى عَلَيْهَا وَدُفِنَتْ (سنن بيهقي: بَابُ الصَّلَاةِ عَلَى مَنْ قَتَلَتْهُ الخُدُودُ، نمبر 6830)
ك وجه:(۱) الحديث لثبوت وَمَنْ قُتِلَ مِنْ الْبُغَاةِ أَوْ قُطَّاعِ الطَّرِيقِ \ عَنْ جَابِرِ بْنِ سَمُرَةَ، قَالَ: " أُتِيَ النَّبِيُّ صلى الله عليه وسلم بِرَجُلٍ قَتَلَ نَظْسَهُ بِمَشَاقِصَ فَلَمْ يُصَلِ عَلَيْهِ (سنن بيهقي: بَابُ الصَّلَاةِ عَلَى مَنْ قَتَلَ نَفْسَةَ غَيْرَ مُسْتَحِلَّ لِقَتْلِهَا ، نمبر 6833)
اصول: اگر کسی شخص کو حربی یا باغی یا پھر چور مار ڈالیں تو وہ شخص بھی شہید کے حکم میں ہے۔ اصول شہر میں جو مقتول ملے تو وہ شہید نہیں ہے الا یہ کہ شہادت کی کوئی علامت ظاہر ہو جائے۔
Chapter of the Martyr. His blood is not washed from him, nor are his clothes removed; the fur coat, khuff (leather socks), turban, and weapons are removed. And one who is murtath (lingers after battle) is washed. Al-irtithath is that he eats, drinks, treats himself, remains alive until the time of a prayer passes while conscious, or is moved from the battlefield while conscious. And one killed in a prescribed punishment (hadd) or retaliation (qisas) is washed and prayed over. And one killed among the rebels (baghi) or highway robbers (qutta' al-tariq) is not prayed over nor washed. [Hadith proofs follow] Principle: If a person is killed by a harbi (enemy combatant), a baghi (rebel), or a thief, then that person is also in the ruling of a martyr. Principle: One who is found killed in the city is not a martyr unless some sign of martyrdom appears.
Source pages p. 186

Commentary
This passage continues the chapter on the martyr, providing specific practical rulings. First, the martyr's blood is not washed off, and his clothes are not removed, except for items like fur coats, khuff (leather socks), turbans, and weapons. Second, if the wounded person is 'murtath' — meaning he eats, drinks, receives treatment, remains conscious through a full prayer time, or is moved from the battlefield while conscious — he loses the special status and is washed and prayed over as a normal deceased. Third, those executed for hadd offenses (e.g., stoning for adultery) or qisas (retaliation) are washed and the funeral prayer is offered; they are not considered martyrs. Fourth, rebels (baghi) and highway robbers (qutta' al-tariq) who are killed are not washed nor is prayer offered over them, as they are considered sinful aggressors. The hadith proofs support each ruling: the martyr of Uhud were buried with blood and clothes (except iron and leather); the story of Umar's assassination shows that the murder victim is washed; the Ghamidiyyah who was stoned was prayed over; and a suicide was not prayed over. The Urdu summary adds that one killed by a harbi, baghi, or thief is considered a martyr, but one found killed in the city is not unless signs of martyrdom are present.

Key Terms
بُغَاة (bughāt): Rebels who rebel against the legitimate Muslim ruler with a valid interpretation (ta'wil).
قُطَّاع الطَّرِيق (qutta' al-tariq): Highway robbers, bandits who attack travelers for robbery.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling for a highway robber killed during a robbery?
A) Washed and prayed over
B) Not washed but prayed over
C) Not washed and not prayed over
D) Buried as a martyr

Key Takeaway
Rebels and highway robbers killed in the act are not washed nor is the funeral prayer offered, as a deterrent and based on analogy to suicide.

Partial Payment Does Not Release Pawned Items
Ruling on partial payment of debt when two items are pawned

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on partial payment of a debt secured by multiple pawned items and apply it to similar scenarios.

Core Idea
Paying part of a debt does not release any pawned item; the entire pawn secures the full debt.

When a debtor pledges multiple items for a single debt, paying off only a portion of that debt creates a natural question: can the debtor reclaim a proportional share of the pawn? The Hanafi school firmly answers no. In this lesson, we examine the clear ruling from the matn and explore its rationale and practical implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling
Read the Arabic text and translation. The ruling is that the debtor may not take possession of any pawned item until the entire debt is paid.
2
Understand the Scenario
Note the example: two slaves are pawned for a debt of 1000. The debtor pays only the portion corresponding to one slave (500). The text prohibits releasing that slave.
The portion is not defined by the value of the slave but by the pro-rata debt share.
3
Grasp the Principle
In Hanafi law, the pawn (rahn) is an indivisible security for the entire debt. Partial payment does not extinguish the security interest proportionally.
This contrasts with schools that view the pawn as divisible.
4
Apply to Other Cases
Generalize: if a debtor pledges any number of items for one debt, no item can be redeemed until the full debt is satisfied.
E.g., three houses, one debt – paying one-third does not release any house.
5
Note the Difference
Some schools (e.g., Shafi'i) allow proportional release if the debt is divisible. This is a valid ikhtilaf; the Hanafi position is mufta bihi in the school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَمَنْ رَهْن عَبْدَيْنِ بِأَلْفِ فَقَضَى حِصَّةَ أَحَدِهِمَا لَمْ يَكُنْ لَهُ أَنْ يَقْبِضَهُ حَتَّى يُؤَدِّيَ بَاقِيَ الدَّيْنِ
Whoever pledges two slaves for a thousand, then pays the portion of one of them, he may not take possession of that slave until he pays the remainder of the debt.
Source pages p. 344

Commentary
This is a ruling: when multiple items are pledged for a single debt, paying off part of the debt does not release the portion of the pawn corresponding to that payment. The pawn remains entire for the rest of the debt. The creditor retains possession of all pawned items until the full debt is cleared.

Key Terms
حِصَّةَ أَحَدِهِمَا (hiṣṣata aḥadihimā): The portion of debt corresponding to one of the pawned slaves.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If someone pledges two slaves for a debt of 1000 and pays 500, can he take one slave?
A) Yes, corresponding to half the debt
B) No, until the entire 1000 is paid
C) Yes, if the debtor agrees
D) No, he must pay 1000 plus penalty

Key Takeaway
Partial payment of a debt does not release any pawned item; the entire pawn remains held until the full debt is cleared.

Validity of Agency to Sell the Pawn at Maturity
Ruling on the validity of appointing the mortgagee or trustee as agent to sell the pawn.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when a pledgor appoints an agent to sell the pawn at maturity.

Core Idea
Agency to sell the pawn at debt maturity is valid, even if the agent is the mortgagee.

When a debt is secured by a pawn, the creditor (mortgagee) often needs to sell the pawn at maturity to recover the debt. The Hanafi school clarifies that the pledgor (owner) can authorize the mortgagee, a neutral trustee, or any third party to sell it. This agency is valid and binding once authorized.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties
Recognize the pledgor (owner of the pawn), the pawn itself, and the appointed agent (mortgagee, trustee, or other). The agent may be the mortgagee who holds the pawn, a neutral trustee, or anyone else.
The text uses 'al-murqina' (likely a typo for al-murtahin) and 'al-`adl'.
2
Note the condition
The agency is specifically for sale 'at the maturity of the term' (عند حلول الأجل). This timing condition is essential for the validity of the agency.
If the sale occurs before maturity without fresh authorization, the agency does not apply.
3
State the ruling
The agency is valid (جائزة). No obligation is created; the agent may execute the sale to recover the debt upon maturity, but is not forced to do so.
The ruling is straightforward and uncontested within the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فَإِذَا وَكَّلَ الرَّاهِنُ الْمُرْقِنَ، أَوْ الْعَدْلَ، أَوْ غَيْرَهُمَا بِبَيْعِ الرَّهْنِ عِنْدَ حُلُولِ الْأَجَلِ فَالْوَكَالَةُ جَائِزَةٌ
When the pledgor appoints the mortgagee, or the trustee, or someone else to sell the pawn at the maturity of the term, the agency is valid.
Source pages p. 344

Commentary
This ruling permits the pledgor (owner of the pawn) to authorize the mortgagee, a neutral trustee, or a third party to sell the pawn when the debt becomes due. The agency is valid; the agent may execute the sale to recover the debt.

Key Terms
الْمُرْقِنَ (al-murqina): Probably a typo for المرتهن (al-murtahin) meaning mortgagee.
الْعَدْلَ (al-`adl): A neutral, trustworthy person (trustee) holding the pawn.
الْوَكَالَةُ (al-wikala): Agency – the authorization to act on behalf of another.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi ruling, which of the following can the pledgor appoint to sell the pawn at maturity?
A) Only the mortgagee
B) Only a trustee
C) The mortgagee, trustee, or any other person
D) Only a judge

Key Takeaway
The pledgor may validly authorize the mortgagee, trustee, or any person to sell the pawn at debt maturity.

6 min
Agency Stipulated in a Pawn Contract Is Irrevocable
Ruling on the irrevocability of agency when stipulated in the pawn contract

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the revocation of agency when stipulated in a pawn contract and explain the consequences of the pledgor's dismissal or death.

Core Idea
An agency stipulated in a pawn contract is irrevocable—neither dismissal nor the pledgor's death terminates it.

In a pawn (rahn) transaction, the mortgagee often needs an agent to manage or sell the collateral if the debt is not repaid. If the agency is made a condition of the pawn contract itself, it gains a binding force that a separate agency does not have. This lesson examines that special status and its practical implications under Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the condition
Recognise that the ruling concerns an agency (wakalah) that is stipulated as a condition within the pawn contract itself, not a separate appointment.
The Arabic: شَرَطَ الْوَكَالَةَ فِي عَقْدِ الرَّهْنِ
2
State the three consequences of the binding agency
First, the pledgor has no right to dismiss the agent; second, if the pledgor does dismiss, the dismissal is ineffective; third, the pledgor's death also does not terminate the agency.
Each consequence reinforces the irrevocable nature.
3
Note the mortgagee's additional rights
The mortgagee (مرتهن) retains the right to demand repayment of the debt and may detain the pledgor if necessary—this is separate from the agency but related.
The text uses يحبسه به meaning imprisonment for a solvent debtor.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فَإِنْ شَرَطَ الْوَكَالَةَ فِي عَقْدِ الرَّهْنِ فَلَيْسَ لِلرَّاهِنِ عَزْلُهُ عَنْهَا فَإِنْ عَزَلَهُ لَمْ يَنْعَزِلْ وَإِنْ مَاتَ الرَّاهِنُ لَم يَنْعَزِلْ وَلِلْمُرْقَن أَنْ يُطَالِبَ الرَّاهِنَ بِدَيْنِهِ وَيَحْبِسَهُ بِهِ
If he stipulates the agency in the pawn contract, then the pledgor has no right to dismiss him from it; if he dismisses him, he is not dismissed; and if the pledgor dies, he is not dismissed; and the mortgagee has the right to demand the debt from the pledgor and to detain him for it.
Source pages p. 345

Commentary
This ruling addresses an agency that is made a condition in the pawn agreement itself. Unlike a separate agency, this one cannot be revoked unilaterally by the pledgor. Even if the pledgor explicitly dismisses the agent, the dismissal is ineffective. Even the death of the pledgor does not terminate the agency. Additionally, the mortgagee (as agent or in his own right) can demand payment of the debt and may detain the pledgor if necessary.

Key Terms
عَزْلُهُ (`azluhu): Dismissal or revocation of the agent's authority.
يَحْبِسَهُ بِهِ (yaḥbisahu bihī): Detain him for it; i.e., the creditor can have the debtor imprisoned until payment.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What happens if the pledgor dies after stipulating agency in the pawn contract?
A) The agency terminates
B) The agency continues
C) The agent must be reappointed by heirs
D) The pawn becomes void

Key Takeaway
When agency is stipulated in a pawn contract, it becomes an irrevocable condition—neither the pledgor's dismissal nor death can terminate it.

6 min
The Three Causes of Interdiction (Hajr)
Defining three causes of interdiction with Quran and Hadith proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three causes of legal interdiction (hajr) in Hanafi fiqh and identify the evidence from Quran and Sunnah that establishes each cause.

Core Idea
Interdiction restricts a person's capacity to transact due to minority, slavery, or insanity, each proven by clear texts.

This passage opens Kitab al-Hajr by defining the precise grounds on which a person's legal capacity to manage property is restricted. Al-Quduri lists three causes: minority, slavery, and insanity. For each, he provides Quranic verses and hadiths that form the evidentiary basis. Understanding these causes is essential to knowing when a transaction is valid or void.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three causes
List the three causes explicitly mentioned: sighar (minority), riqq (slavery), and junun (insanity).
2
Analyze the Quranic proofs
Read verses 4:6 and 4:5. Notice how they restrict property handling until maturity and sound judgment (rushd), implying interdiction for minors and the foolish.
The term 'foolish' (sufaha') includes minors and others lacking capacity.
3
Analyze the Hadith proofs
Three hadiths are cited: (1) The Prophet placed interdiction on Mu'adh's property for debt. (2) The 'raising of the pen' hadith excludes minors, insane, and sleepers from legal accountability. (3) The hadith restricting divorce, manumission, and sale to what one owns reinforces the concept.
Each hadith addresses a different aspect of capacity or ownership.
4
Note the cross-madhhab difference
The Hanafi school restricts hajr to these three. The Shafi'i school adds safah (foolishness/profligacy) as a fourth cause. Recognize the practical consequence.
This ikhtilaf is legitimate; both aim to protect property.
5
Apply the ruling
Determine that a minor's transaction requires guardian permission, a slave's requires master permission, and an insane person's transaction is absolutely void.
Slavery is a cause, but in many modern contexts it is abrogated; the principle remains for other forms of restricted capacity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كِتَابُ الْحَجْرِ

قَالَ - رَحِمَهُ الله -: الْأَسْبَابُ الْمُوجِبَةُ لِلْحَجْرِ ثَلَاثَةُ: الصَّغَرُ، وَالرّقُ، وَالْجُنُونُ. وَلَا يَجُوزُ تَصَرُّفُ الصَّبِيِّ إِلَّا بِإِذْنِ وَلِيِّهِ، وَلَا يَجُوزُ تَصَرُّفُ الْعَبْدِ إِلَّا بِإِذْنِ سَيِّدِهِ، وَلَا يَجُوزُ تَصَرُّفُ الْمَجْنُونِ الْمَعْلُوبِ عَلَى عَقْلِهِ بِحَالٍ.

وَجْهٌ: (1) الْآيَةُ لِثُبُوتِ الْأَسْبَابِ الْمُوجِبَةِ لِلْحَجْرِ ثَلَاثَةُ الصَّغَرُ: {وَابْتَلُوا الْيَتَامَىٰ حَتَّىٰ إِذَا بَلَغُوا النِّكَاحَ فَإِنْ آنَسْتُم مِّنْهُمْ رُشْدًا فَادْفَعُوا إِلَيْهِمْ أَمْوَالَهُمْ} (سورة النساء، 4 آية 6)

وَجْهٌ: (۲) الْآيَةُ لِثُبُوتِ الْأَسْبَابِ الْمُوجِبَةِ لِلْحَجْرِ ثَلَاثَةُ الصَّغَرُ: {وَلَا تُؤْتُوا السُّفَهَاءَ أَمْوَالَكُمُ الَّتِي جَعَلَ اللَّهُ لَكُمْ قِيَامًا} (سورة النساء، 4 آية 5)

وَجْهٌ: (۱) الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ الْأَسْبَابِ الْمُوجِبَةِ لِلْحَجْرِ ثَلَاثَةُ الصَّغَرُ: عَنِ ابْنِ كَعْبِ بْنِ مَالِكٍ عَنْ أَبِيهِ، أَنَّ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم «حَجَرَ عَلَى مُعَاذٍ مَالَهُ وَبَاعَهُ فِي دَيْنٍ كَانَ عَلَيْهِ» (سنن دارقطني، في الْمَرْأَةِ تُقْتَلُ إِذَا ارْتَدَّتْ، نمبر 4551)

وَجْهٌ: (٢) الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ الْأَسْبَابِ الْمُوجِبَةِ لِلْحَجْرِ ثَلَاثَةُ الصَّغَرُ: عَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ، قَالَ: مُرَّ عَلَى عَلِيِّ بْنِ أَبِي طَالِبٍ فِي مَعْنَى عُثْمَانَ، قَالَ: أَوَ مَا تَذْكُرُ أَنَّ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم قَالَ: «رُفِعَ الْقَلَمُ عَنْ ثَلَاثَةٍ، عَنِ الْمَجْنُونِ الْمَعْلُوبِ عَلَى عَقْلِهِ حَتَّى يَفِيقَ، وَعَنِ النَّائِمِ حَتَّى يَسْتَيْقِظَ، وَعَنِ الصَّبِيِّ حَتَّى يَحْتَلِمَ»، قَالَ: صَدَقْتَ، قَالَ: فَخَلَّى عَنْهَا (سنن أبي داود، باب في المجنون يسرق أو يصيب حدًا، نمبر 4401/ صحيح البخاري، باب لا يرجم المجنون والمجنونة، نمبر 6815)

وَجْهٌ: (۳) الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ الْأَسْبَابِ الْمُوجِبَةِ لِلْحَجْرِ ثَلَاثَةُ الصَّغَرُ: عَنْ عَمْرِو بْنِ شُعَيْبٍ، عَنْ أَبِيهِ، عَنْ جَدِّهِ، أَنَّ النَّبِيَّ صلى الله عليه وسلم قَالَ: «لَا طَلَاقَ إِلَّا فِيمَا تَمْلِكُ، وَلَا عِتْقَ إِلَّا فِيمَا تَمْلِكُ، وَلَا بَيْعَ إِلَّا فِيمَا تَمْلِكُ»، زَادَ ابْنُ الصَّبَّاحِ: «وَلَا وَفَاءَ نَذْرٍ إِلَّا فِيمَا تَمْلِكُ» (سنن أبي داود، باب في الطلاق قبل النكاح، نمبر 2190)

اصول: معاملہ کرنے کا مدار عقل ہے، اسلئے جن کو عقل نہیں انکو معاملہ کا اختیار نہیں، یا معاملہ موقوف رہے گا۔
Book of Interdiction. He (the author) said - may Allah have mercy on him -: The causes necessitating interdiction are three: minority, slavery, and insanity. The transaction of a minor is not permissible except with the permission of his guardian; the transaction of a slave is not permissible except with the permission of his master; and the transaction of an insane person who is overcome in his mind is not permissible at all. Proof (1): The verse for establishing the causes necessitating interdiction, three: minority: {And test the orphans until they reach the age of marriage; if you perceive in them sound judgment, deliver to them their property} (Surah an-Nisa, 4:6). Proof (2): The verse for establishing the causes necessitating interdiction, three: minority: {And do not give the foolish your property which Allah has made for you a means of support} (Surah an-Nisa, 4:5). Proof (1): The hadith for establishing the causes necessitating interdiction, three: minority: from Ibn Ka'b b. Malik from his father that the Messenger of Allah ﷺ placed an interdiction on the property of Mu'adh and sold it for a debt that was upon him (Sunan al-Daraqutni, no. 4551). Proof (2): The hadith: from Ibn Abbas, who said: 'Ali b. Abi Talib passed by concerning the affair of Uthman, and said: Do you not remember that the Messenger of Allah ﷺ said: The pen is raised from three: from the insane person overcome in his mind until he recovers, from the sleeper until he wakes, and from the minor until he reaches puberty?' He said: 'You have spoken the truth.' He said: 'So he released her.' (Sunan Abi Dawud, no. 4401; Sahih al-Bukhari, no. 6815). Proof (3): The hadith: from Amr b. Shu'ayb, from his father, from his grandfather, that the Prophet ﷺ said: 'There is no divorce except in what you own, no manumission except in what you own, and no sale except in what you own.' Ibn al-Sabbah added: 'And no fulfillment of a vow except in what you own.' (Sunan Abi Dawud, no. 2190). Principle: The basis of transactions is intellect; therefore, those who have no intellect have no authority over transactions, or the transaction is suspended.
Source pages p. 348

Commentary
This passage introduces Kitab al-Hajr (The Book of Interdiction) and states the foundational ruling: the causes that necessitate legal interdiction (hajr) are three: minority (sighar), slavery (riqq), and insanity (junun). Al-Quduri explains that a minor cannot enter into any transaction without the permission of his guardian (wali). A slave cannot transact without the permission of his master (sayyid). An insane person—one whose intellect is completely overcome—cannot transact at all, under any circumstances. This establishes a complete restriction of legal capacity (ahliyyat al-ada') for these individuals. The text then provides extensive proofs (wujuh) from both the Quran and Sunnah to support this ruling. The first Quranic proof (4:6) commands testing orphans and only releasing their property upon reaching marriageable age and demonstrating sound judgment (rushd), implying a restriction (hajr) on their property until then. The second Quranic proof (4:5) prohibits giving property to the foolish (sufaha'), which encompasses minors and those lacking sound management. The hadith proofs include: (1) the Prophet placing interdiction on Mu'adh's property for a debt, establishing the principle of hajr for financial protection; (2) the famous hadith raising the pen from three: the minor, the insane, and the sleeper, indicating that their actions are not legally effective; (3) the hadith restricting divorce, manumission, and sale to what one owns, implying that those who do not own themselves (slaves) or lack capacity (minors, insane) cannot effect such contracts. The Urdu principle (usul) at the end summarizes: transactions revolve around intellect; those without it either have no authority or their transactions are suspended until permission is granted.

Key Terms
الْحَجْر (al-hajr): A legal restriction preventing a person from disposing of his property or entering into transactions due to a deficiency in capacity.
الصَّغَر (al-sighar): Minority; the state of being a child who has not reached puberty, resulting in restricted legal capacity.
الرّق (al-riqq): Slavery; the legal status of being a slave, which restricts the slave's capacity to own property or transact without the master's permission.
الْجُنُون (al-junun): Insanity; a mental disorder that completely overcomes the intellect, resulting in total restriction of legal capacity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which of the following is NOT a cause for legal interdiction (hajr)?
A) Minority (sighar)
B) Slavery (riqq)
C) Insanity (junun)
D) Profligacy (safah)

Key Takeaway
Interdiction (hajr) is restricted to three causes — minority, slavery, insanity — each supported by clear textual evidence from Quran and Sunnah.

The Three Causes of Hajr and Their Effects on Capacity
States the three causes of interdiction and their general effects on capacity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three causes of legal interdiction (hajr) and apply the rules regarding the validity of contracts, torts, and verbal declarations for minors, the insane, and slaves.

Core Idea
Hajr protects property: minors, the insane, and slaves lack full capacity for statements but remain liable for actions.

This passage from Kitab al-Hajr introduces the three causes that necessitate placing a person under legal interdiction: minority, insanity, and slavery. It then explains the key consequence: these causes restrict the person's verbal declarations (contracts, divorces, etc.) but not their liability for harmful acts. The slave receives a distinct treatment—his statements bind himself but not his master.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three causes of hajr
Read the first sentence and list the three causes: الصغر (minority), الجنون (insanity), الرق (slavery).
These are the only causes in the Hanafi school; other schools add prodigality (safah).
2
Understand the guardian's option
When an interdicted person makes a sale or purchase, the guardian has a choice: ratify if beneficial, or rescind. This protects the ward's interest.
The transaction is not automatically void; it is suspended on the guardian's approval.
3
Distinguish between statements and actions
The text says 'these three meanings necessitate interdiction in statements, not in actions.' This means the person's verbal acts (contracts, confessions, divorce, manumission) are invalid, but they remain liable for torts (e.g., destroying property).
Liability for harm is based on action, not capacity; even a minor must compensate for damage.
4
Apply the rule to minors and the insane
Their contracts, confessions, divorces, and manumissions are void. No legal effect arises from their declarations.
This is because they lack 'ahliyyat al-ada' (capacity to execute).
5
Apply the rule to the slave
A slave's statements are effective regarding his own right (e.g., his own divorce or manumission) but not regarding his master's right (e.g., he cannot incur financial obligations on the master's behalf).
The slave has partial capacity: he can act for himself but cannot bind his master.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الأسباب الموجبة للحجر ثلاثة: الصغر والجنون والرق. ومن باع من هؤلاء شيئًا أو اشتراه فالولي بالخيار إن شاء أجازه إذا كان فيه مصلحة وإن شاء فسخه. وهذه المعاني الثلاثة توجب الحجر في الأقوال دون الأفعال. والصبي والمجنون لا تصح عقودهما ولا إقرارهما ولا يقع طلاقهما ولا عتاقهما وإن أتلفا شيئًا لزمهما ضمانه. فأما العبد فأقواله نافذة في حق نفسه غير نافذة في حق مولاه.
The causes that necessitate interdiction are three: minority, insanity, and slavery. And whoever among these sells something or buys it, the guardian has the option: if he wishes, he may ratify it if there is benefit in it, and if he wishes, he may rescind it. And these three meanings necessitate interdiction in statements, not in actions. And the minor and the insane: their contracts are not valid, nor their confessions, nor does their divorce occur, nor their manumission. And if they destroy something, they are liable for its guarantee. As for the slave, his statements are effective regarding his own right, but not effective regarding the right of his master.
Source pages p. 349

Commentary
This passage from Kitab al-Hajr (Book of Interdiction) states the three causes that justify placing a person under legal interdiction (hajr): minority (sighar), insanity (junun), and slavery (riqq). It then gives the general ruling: if such a person engages in a sale or purchase, the guardian has the option to ratify or rescind the transaction depending on benefit. Importantly, these three causes only restrict the person's statements (aqwal), not their actions (af'al) — meaning liability for torts (itlaf) remains. For the minor and insane, all verbal declarations (contracts, confessions, divorce, manumission) are void. The slave is different: his statements are effective for himself (e.g., his own divorce) but not binding on his master (e.g., he cannot incur financial obligations on the master's account). The Hanafi madhhab distinguishes clearly between capacity for rights (ahliyyat al-wujub) and capacity for execution (ahliyyat al-ada'). This passage reflects those principles.

Key Terms
الحجر (al-hajr): Legal interdiction preventing a person from executing certain actions due to lack of capacity.
السفيه (al-safih): A person who squanders wealth irrationally, lacking prudence in financial matters.
الصغر (al-sighar): Minority, the state of being under the age of puberty.
الجنون (al-junun): Insanity, loss of reason that prevents valid legal acts.
الرق (al-riqq): Slavery, a legal status that limits capacity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on a sale made by a slave without his master's permission?
A) The sale is void because the slave has no capacity.
B) The sale is valid only if the master ratifies it.
C) The sale is effective regarding the slave's own right but not binding on the master.
D) The sale is invalid unless the slave is a minor.

Key Takeaway
The three causes of hajr (minority, insanity, slavery) restrict a person's verbal declarations (contracts, confessions, etc.) but leave liability for torts intact; the slave's statements bind only himself.

Slave's Confession and Divorce in Hanafi Fiqh
Rulings on a slave's confession for property, hudud, and his divorce

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on a slave's confession for property, hadd, and qisas, and the validity of his divorce, and distinguish which are binding immediately and which are suspended.

Core Idea
A slave's confession for property binds after freedom; for hadd/qisas binds immediately; his divorce is valid; the master cannot divorce the slave's wife.

Slaves in Islamic law have limited legal capacity. This passage from Al-Quduri clarifies four key rulings regarding a slave's confession and his marital affairs. Understanding these distinctions is essential for grasping the Hanafi position on partial capacity (ahliyyat al-ada' naqisa).

Guided Path
1
Identify the acts and their subjects
Note that the passage covers two types of acts by the slave: confession (iqrar) and divorce (talaq), and one act by the master: divorcing the slave's wife.
The slave is the subject of the first three rulings; the master is the subject of the fourth.
2
Distinguish property confession from criminal confession
The property confession (al-mal) is suspended until emancipation; the criminal confession (hadd/qisas) takes effect immediately. Understand why: property involves financial liability, which the slave cannot fulfill currently; hudud involve personal liability.
Hadd includes punishments for crimes like theft and adultery; qisas is retaliation for bodily harm or murder.
3
Analyze the slave's divorce
The slave's divorce of his wife is valid and effective (yanfudh talaquhu). Divorce is a personal act and not dependent on property ownership.
This affirms that the slave has full capacity in matrimonial matters.
4
Analyze the master's divorce of the slave's wife
The master cannot divorce his slave's wife (la yaqa' talaq mawlahu 'ala imra'atihi). The master has no marital authority over the slave's wife.
The wife is married to the slave, not to the master.
5
Synthesize the underlying principle
All rulings flow from the principle that a slave has partial legal capacity: he is capable of personal acts (like divorce, confession to crimes) but not financial obligations that require ownership.
This principle is consistent with the Hanafi view of ahliyyat al-ada' naqisa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن أقر بمال لزمه بعد الحرية ولم يلزمه في الحال. فإن أقر بحد أو قصاص لزمه في الحال. وينفذ طلاقه. ولا يقع طلاق مولاه على امرأته.
If he (the slave) confesses to a property debt, it becomes binding upon him after emancipation, but not binding immediately. If he confesses to a hadd (fixed punishment) or qisas (retaliation), it becomes binding immediately. And his divorce takes effect. And the divorce of his master does not occur upon his (the slave's) wife.
Source pages p. 350

Commentary
This passage details the legal capacity of a slave in financial and criminal matters. The slave's confession to a property debt (iqrar bi mal) is suspended, meaning it only becomes binding after he gains freedom, because during slavery he cannot own property. However, confession to a hadd (e.g., adultery, theft) or qisas (e.g., murder) is binding immediately because these involve the slave's person, not his property. Similarly, the slave's divorce of his wife is valid and effective because talaq is a personal act. Conversely, the master cannot divorce the slave's wife, as the master has no marital authority over her. This reflects the Hanafi principle that the slave has partial capacity (ahliyyat al-ada' naqisa) and his statements are effective in matters concerning himself but not his master.

Key Terms
إقرار (iqrar): A confession or admission of a right or liability.
الحرية (al-hurriyyah): Emancipation from slavery.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A slave confesses to stealing (hadd). When does this confession become binding according to the Hanafi school?
A) Immediately.
B) Only after his emancipation.
C) Only if his master agrees.
D) Never.

Key Takeaway
A slave's confession is treated differently based on whether it concerns property (suspended) or his person (immediate), and his divorce is valid while the master's divorce of the slave's wife is not.

Hajr on the Prodigal: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on hajr al-safih

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on interdiction of the prodigal and explain the thamarah al-khilaf in practical terms.

Core Idea
A free adult prodigal's capacity is full for Abu Hanifa but restricted for the Sahibayn.

The issue of whether a free adult who squanders wealth (safih) should be interdicted (hajr) is a classical intra-Hanafi dispute. This passage from Al-Quduri's Mukhtasar captures the divergence between Abu Hanifa and his two famous students. Understanding this ikhtilaf reveals how legal capacity (ahliyyah) interacts with public interest.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core legal issue
The passage asks: Should a free adult prodigal (safih) be placed under legal interdiction (hajr) regarding his property?
The key terms are 'safih' (wasteful) and 'hajr' (interdiction).
2
State Abu Hanifa's position
Abu Hanifa rules that no interdiction is imposed. His transaction is valid even if wasteful. However, for a minor who reaches puberty without prudence (ghayr rashid), property is withheld until age 25, but his transactions before that are still valid.
This is an exception based on minority status, not on foolishness alone.
3
State the Sahibayn's position
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad rule that the prodigal should be interdicted and prevented from disposing of property unless the judge finds benefit.
Their view emphasizes protection of wealth (hifz al-mal).
4
Analyze the basis of each view
Abu Hanifa bases his ruling on full legal capacity of a free adult sane person. The Sahibayn consider public interest (maslahah) and prevention of harm.
No explicit dalil is quoted in the passage; it is a difference of interpretive priority.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf and mufta bihi
Under Abu Hanifa, the prodigal's sales are valid and binding; under the Sahibayn, they are subject to cancellation unless beneficial. The later school adopts the Sahibayn's view as the operative ruling.
The practical difference affects contracts made by such individuals.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقال أبو حنيفة: لا أحجر على السفيه إذا كان حرًا بالغًا عاقلًا وتصرفه في ماله جائز وإن كان مبذرًا مفسدًا يتلف ماله فيما لا غرض له فيه ولا مصلحة إلا أنه قال: إذا بلغ الغلام غير رشيد لم يسلم إليه ماله حتى يبلغ خمسًا وعشرين سنة فإن تصرف قبل ذلك نفذ تصرفه فإذا بلغ خمسًا وعشرين سنة سلم إليه ماله وإن لم يؤنس منه الرشد. وقال أبو يوسف ومحمد: يحجر على السفيه ويمنع من التصرف في ماله فإن كان فيه مصلحة أجازه الحاكم.
And Abu Hanifa said: I do not impose interdiction on the prodigal if he is free, adult, and sane; and his disposal of his property is valid, even if he is a squanderer and corrupt, wasting his wealth on something that has no purpose or benefit for him. Except that he said: If a boy reaches puberty without being prudent, his property is not handed over to him until he reaches twenty-five years. If he disposes before that, his disposal is valid. But when he reaches twenty-five years, his property is handed over to him, even if prudence is not observed from him. And Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said: Interdiction is imposed on the prodigal, and he is prevented from disposing of his property. If there is benefit in it, the judge may permit it.
Source pages p. 350

Commentary
This is a well-known intra-Hanafi dispute (ikhtilaf) regarding the legal status of a safih (prodigal) — a free adult who squanders wealth irrationally. Abu Hanifa's principle is that a free, adult, sane person has full capacity (ahliyyat al-ada' kamilah) and therefore cannot be interdicted from managing his own property, even if he is wasteful. However, he made an exception for a minor who reaches puberty but lacks prudence (ghayr rashid): his property is withheld until age 25, but any transactions before that age are still valid. After 25, the property is handed over unconditionally. This shows Abu Hanifa's reluctance to restrict capacity based on foolishness alone. The two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) disagreed: they held that the safih should be interdicted to protect his wealth, and any transaction by him may be subject to judicial approval if beneficial. Their view aligns more with public interest. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) in the later Hanafi school is the view of the Sahibayn, especially in the context of financial protection.

Key Terms
السفيه (al-safih): A free adult who squanders wealth without benefit.
الرشد (al-rushd): Prudence and sound judgment in financial matters.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, what is the ruling on a transaction made by a 22-year-old who is not yet prudent?
A) The transaction is void.
B) The transaction is valid.
C) The transaction requires guardian approval.
D) The transaction is suspended until age 25.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school's relied-upon view is the Sahibayn's position that a prodigal should be interdicted, overriding Abu Hanifa's strict capacity principle.

The Hanafi Dispute on Interdicting a Safih (Foolish Adult)
Intra-Hanafi dispute on hajr for a safih

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute over hajr on a safih and identify the mufta bihi position with its rationale.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa leaves the safih free; Sahibayn interdict – the later fatwa sides with protection.

A free adult who is wasteful and foolish (safih) presents a legal dilemma: should the state restrict his financial freedom to protect his wealth? Within the Hanafi school, Imams disagreed. This lesson unpacks their arguments, proofs, and the operative ruling for fatwa today.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act in question is hajr (legal interdiction) over a safih (a free adult who is wasteful). Determine whether hajr is permissible or obligatory according to each Imam.
Hajr restricts the safih's ability to dispose of his property.
2
State Abu Hanifa's position
Abu Hanifa holds that no hajr is imposed on a free adult safih. His transactions are valid, even if he ruins his wealth.
He makes an exception for a non-competent youth: property is withheld until age 25.
3
State the Sahibayn's position
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad hold that the safih is interdicted; his transactions are suspended unless the judge finds benefit.
This view prioritizes protection over freedom.
4
Trace the proofs (dalil)
Both sides rely on the same Quranic verse (4:5) but interpret it differently. Abu Hanifa sees it as a recommendation; Sahibayn see it as a prohibition. Sahibayn also use qiyas with a minor.
Abu Hanifa distinguishes the adult safih from a minor and cites a hadith about a weak-minded man.
5
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: under Abu Hanifa, a safih's sale is immediately valid; under Sahibayn, it is suspended and requires judicial approval.
This affects contract enforcement and property protection.
6
Determine the mufta bihi
Later Hanafi fatwa (e.g., in al-Hidayah) adopts the Sahibayn view as it safeguards the safih's interests.
Thus, in practice, a safih is interdicted.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَقَالَ أَبُو حَنِيفَةَ: لَا أَحْجُرُ عَلَى السَّفِيهِ إِذَا كَانَ حُرًّا بَالِغًا عَاقِلًا وَتَصَرُّفُهُ فِي مَالِهِ جَائِزٌ وَإِنْ كَانَ مُبَشِّرًا مُفْسِدًا يُتْلِفُ مَالَهُ فِيمَا لَا غَرَضَ لَهُ فِيهِ وَلَا مَصْلَحَةَ إِلَّا أَنَّهُ قَالَ: إِذَا بَلَغَ الْغُلَامُ غَيْرَ رَشِيدٍ لَمْ يُسَلَّمْ إِلَيْهِ مَالُهُ حَتَّى يَبْلُغَ خَمْسًا وَعِشْرِينَ سَنَةً فَإِنْ تَصَرَّفَ قَبْلَ ذَلِكَ نَفَذَ تَصَرُّفُهُ فَإِذَا بَلَغَ خَمْسًا وَعِشْرِينَ سَنَةً سُلِّمَ إِلَيْهِ مَالُهُ، وَإِنْ لَمْ يُؤْنَسْ مِنْهُ الرُّشْدُ. وَقَالَ أَبُو يُوسُفَ وَمُحَمَّدٌ: يُحْجَرُ عَلَى السَّفِيهِ وَيُمْنَعُ مِنَ التَّصَرُّفِ فِي مَالِهِ فَإِنْ كَانَ فِيهِ مَصْلَحَةٌ أَجَازَهُ الْحَاكِمُ.
Abu Hanifa said: I do not interdict the foolish person when he is free, adult, and sane; his disposal of his property is permissible, even if he is wasteful, corrupt, destroying his property in what is neither beneficial nor in his interest. Except that he said: When a youth reaches puberty without being righteous, his property is not handed over to him until he reaches twenty-five years. If he disposes before that, his disposal is effective. When he reaches twenty-five years, his property is handed over to him, even if no righteousness is perceived from him. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said: The fool is interdicted and prevented from disposing of his property; if there is benefit in it, the judge may permit it.
Source pages p. 350

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the interdiction (hajr) over a free, adult, and sane person who is foolish (safih) with his wealth. Abu Hanifa's position is that such a person is not interdicted; his financial transactions are valid. However, he makes an exception for a youth who reaches puberty without having attained legal competence (rushd). In that case, his property is not handed over to him until he turns 25, but any transactions before that are nonetheless valid. After 25, the property must be given to him regardless of his competence. In contrast, Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad hold that a safih is interdicted and his financial transactions are suspended; they are only permitted if the judge finds benefit in them. This dispute is based on different interpretations of the Quranic verse (4:5) 'Do not give the foolish your property' and the hadith of the Prophet regarding the man with weak understanding. The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position in the late Hanafi school is that of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, as it better protects the interests of the safih.

Key Terms
الْحَجْر (al-hajr): Legal interdiction preventing a person from disposing of their property due to a legal incapacity.
السَّفِيه (al-safih): A person who is wasteful and foolish, lacking sound judgment in financial matters, though adult and sane.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, what happens to a safih's property when he turns 25 years old?
A) It remains under the guardian's control if he is not yet competent.
B) It is handed over to him even if no competence is observed.
C) It is given to the state.
D) He must prove his competence to the judge.

Key Takeaway
The relied-upon Hanafi position is that a free adult safih is interdicted to protect his wealth, following Abu Yusuf and Muhammad.

Rulings on the Safih (Prodigal) Who Has Reached Puberty
Ruling on the legal incapacity of a person who has reached puberty but is not sound in judgment

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on a safih's valid personal acts and financial restrictions, and apply them to scenarios involving marriage, emancipation, zakat, hajj, and wills.

Core Idea
A safih's personal acts are valid, but his wealth is restricted to prevent waste.

In this lesson, we examine the rulings from Al-Quduri's matn on the safih – a person who has reached puberty but lacks sound judgment (rushd). The Hanafi school recognizes that such a person has partial legal capacity: acts like marriage and freeing slaves are valid, but financial disposals are limited to necessities and obligations. Understanding these distinctions is crucial for correctly handling cases involving financially irresponsible adults.

Guided Path
1
Identify who is a safih
A safih is an adult who has reached puberty but is not rashid (sound in judgment). The legal restrictions apply only after this status is established by the judge or guardian.
Safah (prodigality) is a condition of financial mismanagement, not mental illness.
2
List the valid personal acts
Note that marriage and freeing slaves are valid. Also, making a will for charitable purposes within one-third of his wealth is valid.
Marriage is a personal status act, not purely financial, so it is effective.
3
Recognize the financial restrictions
The safih's wealth is not handed over to him; he cannot dispose of it. However, the guardian must fulfill necessary obligations from it: zakat, maintenance for dependents, and expenses for obligatory Hajj.
The judge ensures Hajj expenses are given to a trustee, not directly to the safih.
4
Understand the limitation on mahr and wills
If the safih marries and names a mahr, only the mahr al-mithl is binding; excess is void. His will for charity is valid only up to one-third of his wealth.
These limits protect the safih from excessive financial commitments.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كِتَابُ الْحَجْرِ وَإِنْ أَعْتَقَ عَبْدًا نَفَذَ عِتْقُهُ وَكَانَ عَلَى الْعَبْدِ أَنْ يَسْعَى فِي قِيمَتِهِ فَإِنْ تَزَوَّجَ امْرَأَةً جَازَ نِكَاحُهُ وَإِنْ سَمَّى لَهَا مَهْرًا جَازَ مِنْهُ مِقْدَارُ مَهْرٍ مِثْلِهَا وَبَطَلَ الْفَاضِلُ وَقَالَ فِيمَنْ بَلَغَ غَيْرَ رَشِيدٍ لَمْ يُدْفَعْ إِلَيْهِ مَالُهُ أَبَدًا حَتَّى يُؤْنَسَ مِنْهُ الرُّشْدُ وَلَا يَجُوزُ تَصَرُّفُهُ فِيهِ وَتُخْرَجُ الزَّكَاةُ مِنْ مَالِ السَّفِيهِ وَيُنْفَقُ عَلَى أَوْلَادِهِ وَزَوْجَتِهِ وَمَنْ تَجِبُ عَلَيْهِ نَفَقَتُهُ مِنْ ذَوِي أَرْحَامِهِ فَإِنْ أَرَادَ حَجَّةَ الْإِسْلَامِ لَمْ يُمنَعْ مِنْهَا وَلَا يُسَلِّمُ الْقَاضِي النَّفَقَةَ إِلَيْهِ وَيُسَلِّمُهَا إِلَى ثِقَةٍ مِنْ الْحَاجَ يُنْفِقُهَا عَلَيْهِ فِي طَرِيقِ الْحَجَ فَإِنْ مَرِضَ فَأَوْصَى بِوَصَايَا مِنْ الْقُرَبِ وَأَبْوَابِ الخَيْرِ جَازَ ذَلِكَ فِي ثُلُثِ مَالِهِ
Book of Hajr (Legal Incapacity). And if he frees a slave, his emancipation is effective, and the slave must work to pay his value. And if he marries a woman, his marriage is valid, and if he names a mahr for her, an amount equivalent to her mahr mithl is valid from him, and the excess is void. And he said: Regarding one who has reached puberty but is not sound in judgment, his wealth is never handed over to him until sound judgment is perceived from him. And his disposition over it is not permissible. And zakat is taken out from the wealth of the safih, and expenditure is made on his children, his wife, and those of his relatives whose maintenance is obligatory upon him. And if he desires the Hajj of Islam, he is not prevented from it, but the judge does not hand over the expenses to him; rather, he hands them over to a trustworthy person from the pilgrims who spends them on him on the road to Hajj. And if he becomes ill and makes wills of charitable acts and good deeds, that is valid within one-third of his wealth.
Source pages p. 351

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement from the matn of Al-Quduri on the book of Hajr. It addresses the legal status of a safih – a person who has reached the age of puberty (bulugh) but is not rashid (sound in judgment). The text establishes several key points: First, if such a person frees a slave, the emancipation is effective, but the slave must work to compensate his value (sa'y fi qimatihi). Second, if he marries, the marriage is valid, but the mahr he specifies is limited to the mahr mithl (the appropriate mahr for a woman of her status); any excess is void. This is because the safih is considered to have limited capacity in financial matters but full capacity in personal status (like marriage). Third, the safih's wealth is not handed over to him at all until he demonstrates rushd (sound judgment). He cannot dispose of his property. However, the state (or guardian) takes care of his religious obligations: zakat is paid from his wealth, and maintenance (nafaqah) for his dependents (children, wife, and certain relatives) is provided. If he wants to perform the obligatory Hajj, he is not prevented, but the judge does not give him the expenses directly; instead, they are given to a trustworthy person to spend on him. Finally, if he is ill and makes a will for charitable acts, it is valid only within one-third of his wealth, as per the general rule for wills. These rulings reflect the Hanafi principle that the safih is not totally incompetent but his financial transactions are restricted to protect his wealth and fulfill necessary obligations.

Key Terms
السَّفِيه (al-safih): A person who has reached puberty but is not sound in judgment (non-rashid), thus legally restricted in financial matters.
الرُّشْد (al-rushd): Sound judgment and ability to manage one's financial affairs properly.
مَهْرُ الْمِثْل (mahr al-mithl): The appropriate dower for a woman of her status, considering her family, beauty, etc.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Al-Quduri, what happens if a safih (non-rashid adult) marries and names a mahr greater than the mahr al-mithl?
A) The entire marriage is invalid.
B) The marriage is void but the mahr is paid in full.
C) The marriage is valid, the mahr al-mithl is binding, and the excess is void.
D) The marriage is suspended until the wali approves.

Key Takeaway
A safih has limited financial capacity—personal acts like marriage are valid, but his wealth is protected; obligations like zakat and maintenance are fulfilled from it, and his will is limited to one-third.
