Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Acknowledgment of Counterfeit Coins
Clarifies Hanafi ikhtilaf on whether an acknowledgment specifying counterfeit coins is accepted.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding the debtor's qualification of coins as counterfeit, and identify the practical difference between connected and separate statements.

Core Idea
In Hanafi law, the creditor's claim of good coins prevails unless the debtor's qualification is made in one connected statement.

This passage presents an intra-madhhab ikhtilaf on the credibility of a debtor's acknowledgment when he describes the coins as counterfeit. Abu Hanifa consistently trusts the creditor's assertion that the coins are genuine, binding the debtor to pay good coins. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani introduce a nuance: if the debtor mentions 'counterfeit' in the same breath as the acknowledgment (connected), he is believed; if he states it later in a separate statement, he is not. This distinction reflects deeper principles about the unity of the acknowledgment and the burden of proof in claims of defective payment.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
The debtor acknowledges a debt of 1000 from the price of goods and adds that the coins are counterfeit (zuyuf). The creditor claims they are genuine (jiyad).
2
State Abu Hanifa's position
Abu Hanifa holds that the creditor's claim of genuine coins is always binding; the debtor must pay good coins regardless of how the qualification was phrased.
This is a strict rule protecting the creditor.
3
State Sahibayn's position
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad differentiate: if the debtor said 'counterfeit' in the same connected utterance (mawsul), he is believed; if he said it separately (mafsul), he is not believed.
The key is whether the qualification is part of the original acknowledgment.
4
Identify the key distinction
The distinction hinges on the unity of the statement. A connected statement suggests the debtor is describing the actual coins; a separate statement may appear as an afterthought or excuse.
Hanafi usul considers mawsul to carry more evidentiary weight.
5
Note the practical consequence
Under Abu Hanifa, the debtor always pays good coins. Under Sahibayn, if the debtor was careful to include the qualification in one breath, he may pay counterfeit coins.
The mufta bihi is not specified in the text; later scholars may prefer one view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِنْ قَالَ لَهُ عَلَيَّ أَلْفٌ مِنْ ثَمَنِ مَتَاعِ وَهِيَ زُيُوفٌ وَقَالَ الْمُقَرُّ لَهُ هِيَ جِيَادٌ لَزِمَهُ الْحِيَادُ فِي قَوْلِ أبي حَنِيفَةَ. وَقَالَ أَبُو يُوسُفَ وَمُحَمَّدٌ إِنْ قَالَ ذَلِكَ مَوْصُولًا صُدِقَ، وَإِنْ قَالَهُ مَفْصُولًا لَا يُصَدَّقُ
And if he said: for him upon me a thousand from the price of goods and they are counterfeit, and the acknowledged party said they are genuine, then the genuine is binding in the view of Abu Hanifa. And Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said: if he said that connectedly (in one statement), he is believed; if he said it separately, he is not believed.
Source pages p. 360

Commentary
This is an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning the credibility of the acknowledger's description of the debt. Abu Hanifa holds that when the creditor claims the coins are genuine, that claim prevails regardless of how the debtor's statement was phrased. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad distinguish: if the debtor mentions 'counterfeit' in the same breath (connected), he is believed; if he mentions it later in a separate statement, he is not believed. The text does not specify which view is mufta bihi.

Key Terms
زيوف (zuyuf): Counterfeit or defective coins (plural of zayf).
جياد (jiyad): Genuine, good coins.
موصول (mawsul): Said in one connected statement, as part of the same acknowledgment.
مفصول (mafsul): Said separately, in a subsequent statement.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, if the debtor says the coins are counterfeit but the creditor says they are genuine, what is the ruling?
A) The debtor is believed
B) The creditor is believed
C) It depends on connection
D) Both are believed equally

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, the credibility of a debtor's qualification on the quality of coins depends on whether it was made in the same connected statement (mawsul) or separately (mafsul), with Abu Hanifa always favoring the creditor.

Default Inclusions in Acknowledgment of Composite Items: Ring, Sword, Bridal Tent
Defines default components for acknowledged composite items.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the default components included when acknowledging a ring, sword, or bridal tent according to Hanafi law.

Core Idea
Acknowledgment of a composite item includes its essential and customary components unless excluded.

When you acknowledge ownership of a composite object to another person, what exactly do you transfer? This lesson covers three specific items—ring, sword, and bridal tent—and the default components that automatically accompany them per the Hanafi school. Understanding this principle prevents disputes over what is owned.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its legal effect
The act is acknowledging (iqrar) that a composite item belongs to another. The legal effect is transfer of ownership of that item and its default components.
Acknowledgment is a unilateral declaration; it does not require acceptance.
2
List the three composite items
The passage gives three examples: ring (khatam), sword (sayf), and bridal tent (hajalah).
3
For each item, enumerate the included components
Ring: metal band (khalqah) and gemstone (fass). Sword: blade (nasl), hilt (hifn), and belt (hama'il). Bridal tent: poles ('idan) and covering (kiswah).
These are the customary parts of each item.
4
Derive the general principle
Acknowledgment of a composite includes its essential and customary components (e.g., for a ring, both band and gem are integral). If the acknowledger excludes a component, it is not included.
The rule is based on custom ('urf) and part-whole reasoning.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَمَنْ أَقَرَّ لِغَيْرِهِ بِخَاتَمِ فَلَهُ الْخَلْقَةُ، وَالْفَصُّ وَإِنْ أَقَرَّ لَهُ بِسَيْفِ فَلَهُ النَّصْلُ، وَالْحِفْنُ ، وَالْحَمَائِلُ وَمَنْ أَقَرَّ بِحَجَلَةٍ فَلَهُ الْعِيدَانُ، وَالْكِسْوَةُ
And whoever acknowledges to another a signet ring, then he has the band and the gem. And if he acknowledges to him a sword, then he has the blade, the hilt, and the sword belt. And whoever acknowledges a bridal tent, then he has the poles and the covering.
Source pages p. 360

Commentary
This passage sets default inclusions when someone acknowledges ownership of a composite object. For a ring (khatam), acknowledgment includes the metal band (khalqah) and the gemstone (fass). For a sword (sayf), it includes the blade (nasl), the hilt (hifn), and the belt (hama'il). For a bridal tent (hajalah), it includes the wooden poles ('idan) and the cloth covering (kiswah). The principle is that acknowledgment of the whole includes its essential parts and customary accessories, unless explicitly excluded.

Key Terms
خاتم (khatam): A signet ring, typically with a metal band and a gemstone.
حجلة (hajalah): A bridal tent or canopy, consisting of poles and cloth.
النصل (al-nasl): The blade of a sword.
الخَلْقَة (al-khalqah): The metal band of a ring.
الفَصّ (al-fass): The gemstone of a ring.
الحِفْن (al-hifn): The hilt of a sword.
الحَمَائِل (al-hama'il): The sword belt or baldric.
العِيدَان (al-'idan): The wooden poles of a tent.
الكِسْوَة (al-kiswah): The cloth covering of a tent.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway

Ruling on Acknowledgment of Pregnancy Debt: Specificity vs Ambiguity
Ruling with proof on acknowledgment of pregnancy debt.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition for a valid acknowledgment of a pregnancy debt according to Abu Yusuf and explain why ambiguity (ibham) invalidates it.

Core Idea
An acknowledgment of a pregnancy debt is valid only if its cause is specified; ambiguity renders it void.

This lesson addresses a unique scenario in Hanafi fiqh: acknowledging a debt arising from pregnancy (e.g., dowry). The ruling attributed to Abu Yusuf draws a sharp distinction between specifying the cause and leaving it ambiguous. We will examine the ruling, its underlying logic, and the hadith proofs cited.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is acknowledging a debt related to pregnancy (haml). The ruling: valid if cause specified (e.g., bequest or inheritance), invalid if ambiguous.
2
Locate the authority
This ruling is attributed to Imam Abu Yusuf, one of the two principal students of Abu Hanifa. It may represent a specific viewpoint within the Hanafi school.
3
Understand the key concept: Ibham
Ambiguity in the acknowledgment prevents clear determination of the debt's validity. Hanafi law requires sufficient clarity in acknowledgments.
4
Examine the dalil
Two hadith are cited: the hadith of Ali about distributing sacrificial animals, and the hadith of Safiyyah about the Prophet clarifying her identity. The connection is that they emphasize clarity and avoiding ambiguity.
The hadith proofs are loosely connected; this may reflect a footnote issue.
5
Note the epistemological weight
This ruling is from the nawadir (rare transmissions) of Abu Yusuf, not from Zahir al-Riwayah. Its operative status for fatwa is unclear.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِنْ قَالَ حِمْلٍ فَلَانَةَ عَلَيَّ أَلْفُ دِرْهَم فَإِنْ قَالَ أَوْصَى بِمَا فُلَانٌ، أَوْ مَاتَ أَبُوهُ فَوَرِثَهُ فَالْإِقْرَارُ صَحِيحٌ وَإِنْ أَبْهَمَ الْإِقْرَارَ لَمْ يَصِحَ وَهَذَا عِنْدَ أَبِي يُوسُفَ 19 وجه: (1) الحديث لثبوت أَنَّ عَلِيًّا له أَخْبَرَهُ: «أَنَّ النَّبِيَّ صلى الله عليه وسلم أَمَرَهُ أَنْ يَقُومَ عَلَى بُدْنِهِ، وَأَنْ يَقْسِمَ بُدْنَهُ كُلَّهَا، حُومَهَا وَجُلُودَهَا وَجِلَالَهَا، وَلَا يُعْطِيَ فِي جِزَارَهَا شَيْئًا»، بخاري شريف ، بَابٌ : يُتَصَدَّقُ بِجُلُودِ الْهَدْيِ، نمبر 1717) ٢٠ وجه: (1) الحديث لثبوت وَإِنْ قَالَ حِمْلِ فُلَانَةَ عَلَيَّ أَلْفُ دِرْهَمٍ أَنَّ صَفِيَّةَ زَوْجَ النَّبِيِّ أَخْبَرَتْهُ: «أَنَّهَا جَاءَتْ إِلَى رَسُولِ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم تَزُورُهُ فِي اعْتِكَافِهِ فِي الْمَسْجِدِ فِي الْعَشْرِ الْأَوَاخِرِ مِنْ رَمَضَانَ فَتَحَدَّثَتْ عِنْدَهُ سَاعَةً، ثُمَّ قَامَتْ تَنْقَلِبُ، فَقَامَ النَّبِيُّ الله صلى الله عليه وسلم مَعَهَا يَقْلِبُهَا، حَتَّى إِذَا بَلَغَتْ بَابَ الْمَسْجِدِ عِنْدَ بَابٍ أُمِّ سَلَمَةَ، مَرَّ رَجُلَانِ مِنَ الْأَنْصَارِ، فَسَلَّمَا عَلَى رَسُولِ اللَّهِ ، فَقَالَ هُمَا النَّبِيُّ صلى الله عليه وسلم : عَلَى رِسْلِكُمَا إِنَّمَا هِيَ صَفِيَّةُ بِنْتُ حُيَيٍّ، فَقَالَا: سُبْحَانَ اللهِ يَا رَسُولَ اللَّهِ، وَكَبُرَ عَلَيْهِمَا، فَقَالَ النَّبِيُّ : إِنَّ الشَّيْطَانَ يَبْلُغَ مِنَ الْإِنْسَانِ مَبْلَغَ الدَّمِ، وَإِنِّي خَشِيتُ أَنْ يَقْذِفَ فِي قُلُوبِكُمَا شَيْئًا. (بخاري شريف، بَابٌ : هَلْ يَخْرُجُ الْمُعْتَكِفُ حَوَائِجِهِ إِلَى بَابِ الْمَسْجِدِ، 2035)
And if he said: the pregnancy of so-and-so upon me a thousand dirhams, then if he said 'so-and-so bequeathed' or 'his father died and he inherited it,' the acknowledgment is valid; and if he left the acknowledgment ambiguous, it is not valid. This is according to Abu Yusuf. 19 Proof: (1) The hadith for proof that Ali informed him that the Prophet commanded him to stand over his budn (sacrificial animals) and to distribute all of them, their meat, skins, and coverings, and not to give the butcher anything. (Bukhari, chapter: charity from skins of hadi, no. 1717). 20 Proof: (1) The hadith for proof that the wife of the Prophet Safiyyah informed him that she came to the Messenger of Allah visiting him during his i'tikaf in the mosque in the last ten days of Ramadan, she talked with him for a while, then stood to leave, and the Prophet stood with her to accompany her, until when she reached the door of the mosque at the door of Umm Salamah, two men from the Ansar passed by and greeted the Messenger of Allah. He said to them: 'Take it easy, she is only Safiyyah bint Huyayy.' They said: 'SubhanAllah, O Messenger of Allah,' and it was hard on them. The Prophet said: 'Indeed, Satan reaches from the human as far as the blood, and I feared that he might cast something into your hearts.' (Bukhari, chapter: does the mu'takif exit for his needs to the door of the mosque, no. 2035).
Source pages p. 360

Commentary
This passage deals with acknowledgment of a pregnancy debt (e.g., a dowry or inheritance). The ruling, attributed to Abu Yusuf, states that if the acknowledger specifies the cause (e.g., bequest or inheritance), the acknowledgment is valid; if he leaves it vague (ibham), it is invalid. The text then provides two hadith proofs: (1) the hadith of Ali about distributing sacrificial animals, and (2) the hadith of Safiyyah about the Prophet accompanying her and explaining to the Ansar. The connection of these hadith to the ruling is indirect: the first may illustrate trustworthiness in handling property, the second shows the importance of clarifying ambiguous situations to avoid suspicion. The author uses these as general principles for acknowledging pregnancy.

Key Terms
حمل (haml): Pregnancy; here used metaphorically for a debt or obligation arising from a person's pregnancy (e.g., dowry).
إبهام (ibham): Ambiguity; leaving an acknowledgment unspecified as to cause.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Always valid
B) Only if the cause is specified
C) Only if the amount is less than 1000
D) Never valid

Key Takeaway
An acknowledgment of a pregnancy debt is valid only if its cause is specified, according to Abu Yusuf; ambiguity (ibham) invalidates it.

Acknowledgment of Pregnancy of a Slave-girl or Sheep
Ruling on validity of acknowledging pregnancy of owned property.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling that acknowledging the pregnancy of a slave-girl or sheep is valid and binding.

Core Idea
Acknowledgment of pregnancy in property is valid because the offspring becomes property.

This lesson covers the first part of the passage: the ruling on acknowledging the pregnancy of a slave-girl or sheep. The Hanafi school holds that such an acknowledgment is valid and binding, as the offspring once born are considered property. This ruling underscores the principle that acknowledgments of ownership are effective even for future property with a certain cause.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subject and object
The acknowledgment concerns the pregnancy of a slave-girl or a sheep, made to a specific man (claimant).
2
Determine the legal effect
The text states the acknowledgment is 'sahh al-iqrar wa lazimahu' (valid and binding).
3
Understand the rationale
The offspring is certain to become property upon birth, so acknowledging it is akin to acknowledging a present debt. The certainty of existence (via pregnancy) justifies validity.
Hanafi principle: a known cause (sabab ma'lum) makes future property acknowledgeable.
4
Note the implicit condition
The acknowledgment must be to a specific person (li rajul). Otherwise, it may not be binding as there is no creditor.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الَ وَإِنْ أَقَرَّ بِحَمْلِ جَارِيَةٍ، أَوْ بِحَمْلِ شَاةٍ لِرَجُلٍ صَحَ الْإِقْرَارُ وَلَزِمَهُ وَإِذَا أَقَرَّ الرَّجُلُ فِي مَرَضِ مَوْتِهِ بِدُيُونٍ وَعَلَيْهِ دُيُونٌ لَزِمَتْهُ فِي صِحَتِهِ وَدُيُونٌ لَزِمَتُهُ فِي مَرَضِهِ بِأَسْبَابِ مَعْلُومَةٍ فَدَيْنُ الصَّحَّةِ وَالدَّيْنُ الْمَعْرُوفُ بِالْأَسْبَابِ مُقَدَّمٌ فَإِذَا قُضِيَتْ وَإِنْ لَمْ يَكُنْ عَلَيْهِ دُيُونٌ لَزِمَتْهُ فِي صِحَتِهِ جَازَ إِقْرَارُهُ ۲۳ وَكَانَ الْمُقَرُّ لَهُ أَوْلَى مِنْ الْوَرَثَةِ
He said: And if he acknowledged the pregnancy of a slave-girl or the pregnancy of a sheep to a man, the acknowledgment is valid and binding. And when a man acknowledges debts in his death illness, and he has debts that became binding in health and debts that became binding in illness due to known causes, then the debt of health and the debt known by causes are given precedence. When they are paid off, and if he does not have debts that became binding in health, his acknowledgment is valid. And the acknowledged party has priority over the heirs.
Source pages p. 361

Commentary
This passage covers two distinct topics. First, acknowledgment of a pregnancy of a slave-girl or sheep is valid and binding. This is because the offspring is considered property once born, so the acknowledgment of ownership is effective. Second, the passage deals with acknowledgments made during a death illness (marad al-mawt). In such cases, debts that were incurred during health and debts with known causes (like loans with witnesses) are given priority over vague or self-serving acknowledgments. If there are no prior debts from health, then the acknowledgment during illness is valid. The acknowledged creditor is preferred over the heirs. The text cites Quran 4:12 and hadith about debt before will as proofs.

Key Terms
الإقرار (al-iqrar): Acknowledgment; a declaration by a person that another has a right against him.
حمل (haml): Pregnancy; the unborn offspring.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Yes, it is valid and binding
C) Yes, but only if the sheep is visibly pregnant
D) No, because sheep are not owned

Key Takeaway
Acknowledgment of pregnancy of a slave-girl or sheep is valid and binding in Hanafi law because the offspring is certain to become property.

Prioritization of Debts During Death Illness
Ruling on priority of debts in death illness and validity of acknowledgments.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that debts from health and debts with known causes are given priority over other acknowledgments in death illness.

Core Idea
In death illness, debts with known causes and health debts take precedence over vague acknowledgments.

This lesson examines the second part of the passage: the ruling on acknowledgments of debts made during a death illness (marad al-mawt). To protect against fraudulent claims that could harm heirs, the Hanafi school distinguishes between debts with clear proofs and those acknowledged without known cause. Debts incurred during health and those with known causes (e.g., loans with witnesses) are given priority. Only after these are paid can other acknowledgments be considered, and if there are no prior health debts, the death-illness acknowledgment is valid, giving the creditor priority over heirs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the context: marad al-mawt
The acknowledgment is made during a terminal death illness, which triggers scrutiny to prevent defrauding heirs.
2
Categorize debts into three types
The debtor may have (1) debts incurred during health (dayn al-sihhah), (2) debts incurred during illness with known causes (e.g., documented loans), and (3) other acknowledgments without known cause.
3
Apply the priority rule
Health debts and illness debts with known causes are given precedence (muqaddam) over other acknowledgments. They are paid first from the estate.
4
Determine validity of the death-illness acknowledgment
If there are no prior health debts, then the acknowledgment made during illness is valid (jaza iqraruhu). The acknowledged creditor is preferred over the heirs.
5
Note the dalil
The Quranic verse (4:12) mentioning debt before will supports the priority of debts. The hadith 'Debt is repaid before the will' also applies.
Dalil is from Quran and Sunnah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الَ وَإِنْ أَقَرَّ بِحَمْلِ جَارِيَةٍ، أَوْ بِحَمْلِ شَاةٍ لِرَجُلٍ صَحَ الْإِقْرَارُ وَلَزِمَهُ وَإِذَا أَقَرَّ الرَّجُلُ فِي مَرَضِ مَوْتِهِ بِدُيُونٍ وَعَلَيْهِ دُيُونٌ لَزِمَتْهُ فِي صِحَتِهِ وَدُيُونٌ لَزِمَتُهُ فِي مَرَضِهِ بِأَسْبَابِ مَعْلُومَةٍ فَدَيْنُ الصَّحَّةِ وَالدَّيْنُ الْمَعْرُوفُ بِالْأَسْبَابِ مُقَدَّمٌ فَإِذَا قُضِيَتْ وَإِنْ لَمْ يَكُنْ عَلَيْهِ دُيُونٌ لَزِمَتْهُ فِي صِحَتِهِ جَازَ إِقْرَارُهُ ۲۳ وَكَانَ الْمُقَرُّ لَهُ أَوْلَى مِنْ الْوَرَثَةِ
He said: And if he acknowledged the pregnancy of a slave-girl or the pregnancy of a sheep to a man, the acknowledgment is valid and binding. And when a man acknowledges debts in his death illness, and he has debts that became binding in health and debts that became binding in illness due to known causes, then the debt of health and the debt known by causes are given precedence. When they are paid off, and if he does not have debts that became binding in health, his acknowledgment is valid. And the acknowledged party has priority over the heirs.
Source pages p. 361

Commentary
This passage covers two distinct topics. First, acknowledgment of a pregnancy of a slave-girl or sheep is valid and binding. This is because the offspring is considered property once born, so the acknowledgment of ownership is effective. Second, the passage deals with acknowledgments made during a death illness (marad al-mawt). In such cases, debts that were incurred during health and debts with known causes (like loans with witnesses) are given priority over vague or self-serving acknowledgments. If there are no prior debts from health, then the acknowledgment during illness is valid. The acknowledged creditor is preferred over the heirs. The text cites Quran 4:12 and hadith about debt before will as proofs.

Key Terms
مرض الموت (marad al-mawt): A terminal illness that typically leads to death, during which legal actions are scrutinized for fraud against heirs.
دين الصحة (dayn al-sihhah): A debt incurred while the person was healthy.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Sick Person's Acknowledgment to an Heir: Invalid Unless Others Confirm
Ruling with two hadith proofs about sick person's iqrar to heir

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a sick person's iqrar to an heir and apply the condition that makes it valid.

Core Idea
A sick person's iqrar to an heir is void unless all other heirs consent.

This lesson examines a key Hanafi ruling in inheritance law: the acknowledgment (iqrar) made by a person during deathbed illness in favor of an heir. The default ruling is invalidity, but it can be saved if the remaining heirs confirm it. We will explore the textual proofs from the Sunnah that establish this rule, grounded in the analogy to the prohibition of a will to an heir.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is iqrar (acknowledgment) by a sick person (marad al-mawt) in favor of an heir. The ruling is batil (void) unless a condition is met.
The condition is the confirmation (tasdiq) of the other heirs.
2
Locate the first dalil
The first hadith from Ibn 'Abbas explicitly states that a will to an heir is not permissible without the consent of the heirs. The Hanafi school analogizes iqrar to a will because both are dispositions that can harm other heirs.
Hadith: 'La yajuzu li-warithin wasiyyatun illa an yasha'a al-warathah.'
3
Locate the second dalil
The second hadith from Ja'far ibn Muhammad prohibits both a will to an heir and an acknowledgment of a debt (in this context, iqrar). This shows the direct link between iqrar and wasiyyah.
Hadith: 'La wasiyyata li-warithin wa la iqrar bi-daynin.'
4
Apply the analogy (qiyas)
Both iqrar and wasiyyah are voluntary dispositions made during illness that reduce the estate available to heirs. Hence, the same rule applies: they require the consent of other heirs.
The 'illa (effective cause) is the potential harm to the rights of other heirs.
5
Note the practical consequence (thamarah)
If the other heirs do not confirm the iqrar, it is void and the acknowledged debt is not enforceable against the estate. If they do confirm, it becomes valid and binding.
This protects the shares of the remaining heirs from unfair depletion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
٢٤ وَإِقْرَارُ الْمَرِيضِ لِوَارِثِهِ بَاطِلٌ إِلَّا أَنْ يُصَدِّقَهُ بَقِيَّةُ الْوَرَثَةِ
وَجْهٌ : (١) الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ وَإِقْرَارُ الْمَرِيضِ لِوَارِثِهِ بَاطِلٌ إِلَّا أَنْ يُصَدِّقَهُ 
عَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ ، قَالَ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم: «لَا يَجُوزُ لِوَارِثِ وَصِيَّةٌ إِلَّا أَنْ يَشَاءَ الْوَرَثَةُ»،(سُنَنُ الدَّارَقُطْنِيِّ، كِتَابُ الْوَصَايَا ، نَمَبَر 4297/سُنَنُ التِّرْمِذِيِّ، بَابُ مَا جَاءَ لَا وَصِيَّةَ لِوَارِثِ، نَمَبَر 2120/سُنَنُ أَبِي دَاوُدَ شَرِيفٍ، بَابُ مَا جَاءَ فِي الْوَصِيَّةِ لِلْوَارِثِ، نَمَبَر 2870)
وَجْهٌ: (٢) الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ وَإِقْرَارُ الْمَرِيضِ لِوَارِثِهِ بَاطِلٌ إِلَّا أَنْ يُصَدِّقَهُ 
عَنْ جَعْفَرِ بْنِ مُحَمَّدٍ عَنْ أَبِيهِ ، قَالَ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم: «لَا وَصِيَّةَ لِوَارِثِ وَلَا إِقْرَارَ بِدَيْنٍ» (سُنَنُ الدَّارَقُطْنِيِّ، كِتَابُ الْوَصَايَا ، غمبَر 4298)
24. And the acknowledgment of the sick person to his heir is invalid unless the rest of the heirs confirm him. Evidence (1): The hadith for establishing that the acknowledgment of the sick person to his heir is invalid unless they verify him: From Ibn 'Abbas, he said: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'A will to an heir is not permissible unless the heirs wish it.' (Sunan al-Daraqutni, Book of Wills, no. 4297; Sunan al-Tirmidhi, Chapter on No Will to an Heir, no. 2120; Sunan Abi Dawud, Chapter on What Came Concerning a Will to an Heir, no. 2870). Evidence (2): The hadith for establishing that the acknowledgment of the sick person to his heir is invalid unless they verify him: From Ja'far ibn Muhammad from his father, he said: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'No will to an heir and no acknowledgment of a debt.' (Sunan al-Daraqutni, Book of Wills, no. 4298).
Source pages p. 362

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling from the Hanafi school regarding the acknowledgment (iqrar) made by a sick person during his deathbed illness (marad al-mawt). The ruling states that such an acknowledgment in favor of an heir is invalid unless the other heirs confirm it. This is because the iqrar is analogous to a will (wasiyyah) to an heir, which is prohibited by the hadith. The first hadith cited from Ibn 'Abbas explicitly states that no will to an heir is valid without the consent of the other heirs. The second hadith further reinforces that there is no will to an heir and no acknowledgment of a debt (in this context). The Hanafi position is that the sick person's iqrar to an heir is considered a disposition that would harm the other heirs' shares, hence it is suspended upon their approval. The passage type is a ruling with proof, where the matn (base text) is followed by two hadith evidences. The commentary follows the author's order: first the ruling, then the evidences. The analytical toolbox includes a Hanafi position box and a dalil block.

Key Terms
إِقْرَار (iqrar): Acknowledgment or confession; a legal declaration by which a person affirms a right of another against himself.
مَرِيض (marid): A sick person, specifically one in marad al-mawt (deathbed illness) where death is imminent and the person is incapacitated.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

C) The acknowledgment is automatically valid if the debt is less than one-third of the estate.
D) The acknowledgment is valid only if the daughter is also a creditor.

Key Takeaway
A sick person's iqrar to an heir is void ab initio unless all other heirs confirm it, protecting their inheritance shares.

Conditions for Acknowledgment of Lineage
Summarizes key rulings on iqrar bi al-nasab.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which a woman's acknowledgment of a child is accepted and apply the rules for acknowledging lineage of non-parents, distinguishing between lineage and inheritance effects.

Core Idea
Acknowledgment of lineage binds only with verification or when no known heir exists.

The Hanafi school places strict conditions on acceptance of lineage admissions to prevent false claims. This passage from Al-Quduri's matn establishes four key rules: a woman's claim requires external support, non-parent lineage acknowledgments are invalid for lineage but may affect inheritance, existing heirs override such claims, and a posthumous acknowledgment of a brother only grants inheritance without lineage. Let's unpack these rulings step by step.

Guided Path
1
Identify the first rule: woman's acknowledgment of a child
The passage states that a woman's claim to a child is not accepted unless either the husband confirms or a midwife testifies to the birth. Note that this is a condition (shart) for the acknowledgment's validity.
The midwife (qabilah) must be a reliable witness; her testimony is sufficient per Hanafi.
2
Identify the second rule: acknowledging a non-parent relative
If someone acknowledges a lineage other than their own parents or children—e.g., a brother or uncle—that acknowledgment is not accepted for establishing lineage (nasab). The text explicitly says 'لم يقبل إقراره في النسب'.
This does not mean the acknowledgment is entirely void; it may have inheritance effects.
3
Understand the inheritance implications
If the person making the acknowledgment has a known heir (close or distant), that heir takes precedence in inheritance over the acknowledged person. Only if there is no known heir does the acknowledged person become entitled to the inheritance.
The passage uses 'وارث معروف' to indicate any recognized legal heir, whether close (e.g., son) or distant (e.g., cousin).
4
Recognize the posthumous acknowledgment scenario
If a father dies and then his son acknowledges a brother, the brother's lineage is not proven, but the brother still shares in the inheritance as an heir. This shows that the acknowledgment creates an inheritance right without establishing actual lineage.
This is a unique Hanafi rule: the acknowledged person inherits as if they were the claimed relative, but only for that specific estate.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كِتَابُ الْإِقْرَارِ وَلَا يُقْبَلُ إِقْرَارُهَا بِالْوَلَدِ إِلَّا أَنْ يُصَدِّقَهَا الزَّوْجُ، أَوْ تَشْهَدَ بِوِلَادَتِهَا قَابِلَةٌ. وَمَنْ أَقَرَّ بِنَسَبٍ مِنْ غَيْرِ الْوَالِدَيْنِ، وَالْوَلَدِ مِثْلُ الْأَخِ، وَالْعَمَّ لَمْ يُقْبَلْ إِقْرَارُهُ فِي النَّسَبِ. فَإِنْ كَانَ لَهُ وَارِثٌ مَعْرُوفٌ قَرِيبٌ، أَوْ بَعِيدٌ فَهُوَ أَوْلَى بِالْمِيرَاثِ مِنَ الْمُقَرِّ لَهُ فَإِنْ لَمْ يَكُنْ لَهُ وَارِثٌ اسْتَحَقَّ الْمُقَرُّ لَهُ مِيرَاثَهُ وَمَنْ مَاتَ أَبُوهُ فَأَقَرَّ بِأَخٍ لَمْ يَثْبُتْ نَسَبُ أَخِيهِ وَيُشَارِكُهُ فِي الْمِيرَاثِ
The Book of Acknowledgment. And the acknowledgment of a woman regarding a child is not accepted unless the husband confirms her, or a midwife testifies to her giving birth. And whoever acknowledges a lineage other than the parents and the child, like the brother and the uncle, his acknowledgment in lineage is not accepted. If he has a known heir, close or distant, that heir is more entitled to the inheritance than the acknowledged person. If he has no heir, the acknowledged person becomes entitled to his inheritance. And whoever's father dies and he acknowledges a brother, the brother's lineage is not established, but he shares with him in the inheritance.
Source pages p. 363

Commentary
This passage from Al-Quduri's matn outlines the Hanafi rulings on acknowledgment of lineage (iqrar bi al-nasab). First, a woman's claim that a child is hers is only accepted if her husband confirms it or a midwife (qabilah) testifies to the birth. This is to prevent false attribution. Second, acknowledging lineage for someone other than one's own parents or children—such as a brother or uncle—is not accepted in terms of establishing lineage (nasab); however, it may affect inheritance. Third, if the acknowledging person has a known heir, that heir takes precedence in inheritance over the acknowledged person. Only if there is no known heir does the acknowledged person inherit. Fourth, if a man dies and his son acknowledges a brother, the brother's lineage is not proven, but he still inherits as if he were a brother. Note: The text does not provide proofs here; those are given in the hadith footnotes.

Key Terms
إقرار (iqrar): Acknowledgment or admission of a right or relationship, here specifically of lineage.
نسب (nasab): Lineage or paternal descent.
قابلة (qabilah): A midwife who assists in childbirth and can testify to the birth.
ميراث (mirath): Inheritance.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if a man acknowledges a brother and has no known heir, what is the result?
A) The brother's lineage is established and he inherits.
B) The brother's lineage is not established, but he inherits.
C) The brother's lineage is not established, and he does not inherit.
D) The acknowledgment is void entirely.

Key Takeaway
Acknowledgment of lineage is accepted only with external verification; otherwise, it may only affect inheritance in the absence of known heirs.
